The Three Deviant Sects: Anadiyya, Indiyya, and La-adriyya
Author enumerates three deviant sects and their doctrines, then assesses them as beyond rational debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the positions of the three deviant sects and why they are considered outside the consensus of rational people, and the extreme nature of the response required.

Core Idea
Three sects deny objective truth, leaving no ground for rational debate.

This passage introduces three sects that fundamentally reject the foundations of knowledge and reality. Understanding their claims helps us appreciate the boundaries of rational discourse in Islamic theology. The author then presents the view that such deniers cannot be reasoned with.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sects
Read the description of each sect and note their core beliefs. The Anadiyya deny objective reality, the Indiyya make truth relative to personal belief, and the La-adriyya embrace radical skepticism.
Notice how each sect undermines a basic principle of knowledge.
2
Understand the author's assessment
The author states that these sects have departed from the consensus of rational people (khārijūna ‘an qawli al-‘uqalā’). Reflect on why this is a serious charge in Islamic theology.
3
Consider the recommended response
Read the quote from the author of al-‘Aqā’id, who says that debating the La-adriyya is futile; the only way is to punish them by fire. This underscores the severity of their deviation.
Think about why rational argument fails with them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عناديَّة يقولون : لا ثبوت لحقيقة من الحقائق، وإنَّما هي أوهام وخيالات كالذي يرى في المنام . وعنديَّة يقولون الشَّخص عند اعتقاده، حتَّى لو اعتقد أنَّ النَّار جَنَّة أو بالعكس لكان كذلك. واللاأدرية يقولون في كل شيء: لا أدري، حتى إنَّه يشكُ نفسه وفي شكّه . وتوضيح الرَّدِّ عليهم مذكور في المطولات. الحقُّ أنَّهم خرجوا عن قول العقلاء، كذا قرَّره المؤلّف. قوله : (عناديَّة) : سمُّوا بذلك لعنادهم ومكابرتهم لأهل الحقِّ . قوله : (يقولون : الشَّخص عند اعتقاده بيان لتسميتهم عنديَّة، وكذا يقال فيما بعده. قوله : (وتوضيح الرَّدِّ عليهم مذكور في المطوّلات): قال صاحب العقائد بعد كلام طويل: (الحقُّ أنَّه لا طريق إلى المناظرة معهم خصوصاً اللا أدرية ؛ لأنَّهم لا يعترفون بمعلوم ليثبت به مجهول، بل الطريق تعذيبهم بالنار ليعترفوا أو يحترقوا)(١).
The Anadiyya say: There is no establishment of any reality, but rather they are illusions and fantasies like what one sees in a dream. The Indiyya say: The person (is) according to his belief, even if he believed that fire is a garden or vice versa, it would be so. The La-adriyya say about everything: I do not know, even to the point that he doubts himself and his doubt. The clarification of the refutation against them is mentioned in the lengthy works. The truth is that they have departed from the saying of the rational people; thus the author has decided. His saying: (Anadiyya) - they are named thus for their obstinacy and invective against the people of truth. His saying: (they say: the person is according to his belief) is an explanation of their naming as Indiyya, and likewise is said regarding what follows. His saying: (And the clarification of the refutation against them is mentioned in the lengthy works): The author of al-Aqa'id said after a lengthy speech: (The truth is that there is no way to debate with them, especially the La-adriyya, because they do not acknowledge any known thing by which an unknown could be proven; rather the way is to punish them with fire so that they either acknowledge or burn.)
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage refutes three deviant sects: the Anadiyya (who deny objective reality), the Indiyya (who make truth relative to belief), and the La-adriyya (radical skeptics). The author first summarises each sect's position, then notes that a full refutation is found in longer works. He asserts that these sects have left the consensus of rational people. The hashia then explains the naming of Anadiyya (from obstinacy) and Indiyya (from relative belief). Finally, he quotes the author of al-Aqa'id, who argues that debating the La-adriyya is futile because they accept no premises; the only effective response is to punish them by fire, so they either admit the truth or burn. This underscores the seriousness of their denial of reality.

Key Terms
عنادية
عندية
لاأدرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think these sects can be refuted through rational debate like other deviant groups.
Correction: The passage shows they are beyond debate because they deny the very basis of knowledge and proof; the only effective response is force.

Checkpoint
What is the recommended response to the La-adriyya according to the author of al-Aqa'id?
A) Debate them with logical proofs
B) Punish them with fire
C) Ignore them completely
D) Accept their skepticism

Key Takeaway
The three sects (Anadiyya, Indiyya, La-adriyya) are considered beyond rational argument, and the only effective response is physical punishment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the description of the Indiyya — that a person is according to his belief, even if he believed fire is a garden — do you ever act as if your subjective feelings define what is true? Where in your life have you treated your preferences as if they were reality, ignoring what Allah has revealed as objective truth?
?
The La-adriyya claim 'I do not know' about everything, even about themselves. Is there an area of Islamic teaching that you have been avoiding by saying 'I don't know' when in reality you fear the implication? What would it cost you to honestly seek knowledge and act on it?
?
The author of al-‘Aqā’id says the only way to deal with those who reject rational discourse is to punish them with fire. Have you ever considered that your own stubbornness or skepticism might be a milder form of the same disease? Will you let the fear of Allah's punishment drive you to submit to the truth today?

The Philosophers' Classification of Temporal and Eternal
The philosophers define two types of temporal and two types of eternal being.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' classification of beings into temporal by essence vs. temporal by time, and eternal by essence vs. eternal by time, and how they differ from the mainstream Islamic theological view.

Core Idea
The philosophers split 'temporal' and 'eternal' based on causation, not just time.

The passage begins by laying out the philosophers' categorization of existence. They divide the created (al-hadith) into two types and the eternal (al-qadim) into two types, using a criterion that differs from the mainstream Sunni position. Understanding these definitions is crucial before examining their emanation theory.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification of temporal beings
Notice the two subcategories: temporal by essence (needs a cause) and temporal by time (preceded by non-existence). Understand the examples.
The philosophers consider the celestial spheres as temporal by essence but not by time.
2
Read the classification of eternal beings
Eternal by essence (no cause needed) is only God; eternal by time (no temporal beginning but caused) applies to the spheres.
This is where the philosophers differ from Ahl al-Sunna.
3
Reflect on the implications
Think about why the philosophers separate time from causation. How does this affect their view of God and creation?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحاصل مذهب الفلاسفة: أنَّ الحادث عـنـدهـم قـسـمـان: حادث بالذات، ويفسرونه بما يحتاج في وجوده إلى مؤثر، سواء سبقه عدم أو لا، فالأول : كأفراد الإنسان، والثَّاني : كالأفلاك؛ فإنَّها محتاجة في وجودها للمؤثر ولم يسبقها عدم، وحادث بالزَّمان، ويفسرونه بما سبق وجوده عدم؛ كأفراد الإنسان والقديم قسمان: قديم بالذات، وهو ما لا يحتاج في وجوده لمؤثر؛ كذات المولى تعالى، وقديم بالزمان، وهو ما لا يسبقه عدم، واحتاج في وجوده لمؤثّر ؛ كالأفلاك فإنَّها عندهم لم يسبقها عدم؛ لأنَّها ناشئة عن العقول بطريق العلة. ويقولون : إنَّ واجب الوجود الله واحد من كل جهة، فلا قدرة له ولا إرادة، ولا صفة له زائدة على الذات والواحد من كلِّ جهة إنَّما ينشأ عنه واحد بطريق العلة، فالواحد الذي ينشأ عنه يقال له : العقل الأوَّل، ثمَّ إِنَّ ذلك العقل متّصف بالإمكان من حيث إنَّ الغير أثر فيه، وبالوجوب فهو قديم لعلَّته، حادث باعتبار ذاته، فنشأ عنه باعتبار الجهة الأولى عقل ثان، ونشأ عنه من الجهة الثَّانية فلك أوَّل، وهو المسمى في لسان الشرع بـ(العرش). ثمَّ إِنَّ هذا العقل الثَّاني متّصف بالإمكان من حيث إنَّ الغير أثر فيه،
The summary of the philosophers' doctrine is that the temporal is of two types according to them: temporal by essence, which they interpret as that which needs an effect for its existence, whether preceded by non-existence or not. The first is like individual humans, and the second is like the celestial spheres, for they need an effect for their existence but were not preceded by non-existence. Temporal by time, which they interpret as that whose existence is preceded by non-existence, like individual humans. The eternal is of two types: eternal by essence, which does not need an effect for its existence, like the essence of the Most High God; and eternal by time, which is not preceded by non-existence but needs an effect for its existence, like the celestial spheres, for according to them they were not preceded by non-existence because they arise from the intellects via the way of causality. And they say that the Necessary Existent, God, is one from every aspect, so He has no power, no will, and no attribute additional to the essence, and the one from every aspect only produces one via the way of causality. So the one produced from Him is called the First Intellect. Then that intellect is qualified with contingency inasmuch as the other has an effect in it, and with necessity, so it is eternal by its cause, temporal in terms of its essence. So from it, by virtue of the first aspect, a second intellect emerged, and by virtue of the second aspect, a first sphere emerged, which is called in the language of the Law the Throne. Then this second intellect is qualified with contingency inasmuch as the other has an effect in it,
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the philosophers' doctrine (مذهب الفلاسفة). It begins by classifying the created (الحادث) into two categories: (1) temporal by essence (حادث بالذات) – that which needs a cause for its existence regardless of temporal precedence – and (2) temporal by time (حادث بالزمان) – that which is preceded by non-existence. Similarly, the eternal (القديم) is two categories: (1) eternal by essence (قديم بالذات) – that which needs no cause, like God – and (2) eternal by time (قديم بالزمان) – that which is not preceded by non-existence but needs a cause, like the celestial spheres. The philosophers then explain that the Necessary Existent (واجب الوجود) is absolutely one, devoid of attributes and will, and from such a one only one can emanate. That emanation is the First Intellect (العقل الأول). The First Intellect is contingent in itself but necessary by its cause, so from it emanates a Second Intellect and the First Sphere (the Throne). The text cuts off while describing the Second Intellect.

Key Terms
حادث بالذات
حادث بالزمان
قديم بالذات
قديم بالزمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All created things are preceded by non-existence.
Correction: The philosophers hold that some created things, like the celestial spheres, are not preceded by non-existence but still require a cause; they call this 'temporal by essence'.

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers, what is 'temporal by essence'?
A) That which is preceded by non-existence
B) That which does not need a cause
C) That which needs a cause for its existence, whether preceded by non-existence or not
D) That which is eternal

Key Takeaway
The philosophers classify beings based on causation and temporal priority, creating four categories that allow them to consider the celestial spheres as caused but eternal in time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If only God is truly independent and uncaused, what created things are you relying on as if they were self-sufficient? How can you redirect your ultimate dependence to God alone?
?
The philosophers describe the celestial spheres as caused but without beginning in time. Does this view challenge your understanding of God's absolute sovereignty and the universe's total dependence on Him at every moment? What does it mean for you to acknowledge that every thing—whether temporal or eternal in time—exists only through God's constant causation?
?
Consider the difference between something that exists by its own essence (only God) and something that exists by another's causation. How does this affect your view of your own existence and your relationship with your Creator? Are you living as if your existence is self-sufficient, or do you recognize your continuous need for God?

The Philosophers' Emanation Scheme: From the One to the First Intellect
The philosophers detail the emanation of the First Intellect from God and the subsequent generation of the second intellect and the first sphere.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' theory of emanation from the One Necessary Existent, leading to the First Intellect and the subsequent generation of multiplicity.

Core Idea
From the absolutely One God, only one thing can emanate: the First Intellect.

After establishing their classification, the philosophers present their cosmology. They assert that God is one from every aspect, lacking attributes and will. From such a simple unity, only a single effect can proceed directly. This effect is the First Intellect, which then becomes the source of multiplicity through its dual aspects.

Guided Path
1
Read the description of God's oneness
Notice that they deny God any attributes or will, saying He is one from every aspect. Understand this premise.
This is a key difference from Islamic theology.
2
Trace the first emanation
From the One, only one proceeds: the First Intellect. Understand why only one can come directly.
The principle is 'from the one, only one proceeds'.
3
Follow the generation of the Second Intellect and First Sphere
The First Intellect has two aspects: contingency (by itself) and necessity (by its cause). From these aspects, a second intellect and the first sphere (Throne) emanate.
The passage is cut off, but the pattern continues.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحاصل مذهب الفلاسفة: أنَّ الحادث عـنـدهـم قـسـمـان: حادث بالذات، ويفسرونه بما يحتاج في وجوده إلى مؤثر، سواء سبقه عدم أو لا، فالأول : كأفراد الإنسان، والثَّاني : كالأفلاك؛ فإنَّها محتاجة في وجودها للمؤثر ولم يسبقها عدم، وحادث بالزَّمان، ويفسرونه بما سبق وجوده عدم؛ كأفراد الإنسان والقديم قسمان: قديم بالذات، وهو ما لا يحتاج في وجوده لمؤثر؛ كذات المولى تعالى، وقديم بالزمان، وهو ما لا يسبقه عدم، واحتاج في وجوده لمؤثّر ؛ كالأفلاك فإنَّها عندهم لم يسبقها عدم؛ لأنَّها ناشئة عن العقول بطريق العلة. ويقولون : إنَّ واجب الوجود الله واحد من كل جهة، فلا قدرة له ولا إرادة، ولا صفة له زائدة على الذات والواحد من كلِّ جهة إنَّما ينشأ عنه واحد بطريق العلة، فالواحد الذي ينشأ عنه يقال له : العقل الأوَّل، ثمَّ إِنَّ ذلك العقل متّصف بالإمكان من حيث إنَّ الغير أثر فيه، وبالوجوب فهو قديم لعلَّته، حادث باعتبار ذاته، فنشأ عنه باعتبار الجهة الأولى عقل ثان، ونشأ عنه من الجهة الثَّانية فلك أوَّل، وهو المسمى في لسان الشرع بـ(العرش). ثمَّ إِنَّ هذا العقل الثَّاني متّصف بالإمكان من حيث إنَّ الغير أثر فيه،
The summary of the philosophers' doctrine is that the temporal is of two types according to them: temporal by essence, which they interpret as that which needs an effect for its existence, whether preceded by non-existence or not. The first is like individual humans, and the second is like the celestial spheres, for they need an effect for their existence but were not preceded by non-existence. Temporal by time, which they interpret as that whose existence is preceded by non-existence, like individual humans. The eternal is of two types: eternal by essence, which does not need an effect for its existence, like the essence of the Most High God; and eternal by time, which is not preceded by non-existence but needs an effect for its existence, like the celestial spheres, for according to them they were not preceded by non-existence because they arise from the intellects via the way of causality. And they say that the Necessary Existent, God, is one from every aspect, so He has no power, no will, and no attribute additional to the essence, and the one from every aspect only produces one via the way of causality. So the one produced from Him is called the First Intellect. Then that intellect is qualified with contingency inasmuch as the other has an effect in it, and with necessity, so it is eternal by its cause, temporal in terms of its essence. So from it, by virtue of the first aspect, a second intellect emerged, and by virtue of the second aspect, a first sphere emerged, which is called in the language of the Law the Throne. Then this second intellect is qualified with contingency inasmuch as the other has an effect in it,
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the philosophers' doctrine (مذهب الفلاسفة). It begins by classifying the created (الحادث) into two categories: (1) temporal by essence (حادث بالذات) – that which needs a cause for its existence regardless of temporal precedence – and (2) temporal by time (حادث بالزمان) – that which is preceded by non-existence. Similarly, the eternal (القديم) is two categories: (1) eternal by essence (قديم بالذات) – that which needs no cause, like God – and (2) eternal by time (قديم بالزمان) – that which is not preceded by non-existence but needs a cause, like the celestial spheres. The philosophers then explain that the Necessary Existent (واجب الوجود) is absolutely one, devoid of attributes and will, and from such a one only one can emanate. That emanation is the First Intellect (العقل الأول). The First Intellect is contingent in itself but necessary by its cause, so from it emanates a Second Intellect and the First Sphere (the Throne). The text cuts off while describing the Second Intellect.

Key Terms
العقل الأوَّل
العقل الثَّاني
فلك أوَّل
العرش
واجب الوجود
العلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God directly creates all things without intermediaries.
Correction: The philosophers hold that from the absolutely One God, only one thing (the First Intellect) proceeds directly; all else emanates through successive intellects and spheres.

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers, what is the first being to emanate from God?
A) The First Intellect
B) The Second Intellect
C) The First Sphere
D) The Throne

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' emanation scheme posits that from the absolutely one God, only one effect, the First Intellect, proceeds, and from it multiplicities arise through its dual aspects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The philosophers reason that God cannot have power or will because that would imply multiplicity in His essence. When you reflect on your own concept of God, do you ever find yourself limiting His attributes to fit your logic? How would your prayer life change if you truly believed God acts only out of necessity, not will?
?
The emanation scheme places a chain of intermediaries between you and God. Have you ever subconsciously placed 'intellects' between you and God—such as your own reasoning, scholars, or worldly systems? What would it take to remove those barriers and approach God directly?
?
If God's direct involvement is reduced to a single, distant act of emanation, then personal connection with Him becomes meaningless. Are there areas of your life where you treat God as a distant first cause rather than a living, responsive Lord? What practical step can you take today to treat Him as nearer?

The Philosophers' Classification of Origination and Eternity
Al-Sawi enumerates the philosophers' four categories of eternity and origination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourfold classification of originated and eternal according to the philosophers (falāsifa), and why they distinguish between essential and temporal origination.

Core Idea
The philosophers divided the originated and eternal into four categories based on essence and time.

The philosophers (falāsifa) developed a sophisticated metaphysical framework to explain the world's relationship with God. Central to this framework is a fourfold classification of things as either originated (ḥādith) or eternal (qadīm), and further subdivided by whether the category relates to essence or time. In this passage, al-Sawi summarizes this classification before delving into the emanation theory.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the definitions and examples for each of the four categories.
2
Compare the two types of originated
Identify the difference between 'originated in essence' and 'originated in time'. Note that the spheres are originated in essence but not preceded by non-existence.
This is key to understanding their cosmology.
3
Reflect on the need for four categories
Ask yourself why the philosophers needed to distinguish between essential and temporal attributes. How does this allow them to claim the world is both caused and eternal?
This connects to the emanation theory in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حدوث العالم أو أنَّ المراد : أَنَّه يجب له الحدوث كما يجب لمُحدِثه القِدَم، فلا يرد أنَّ حدوثه لا يقول به الفلسفي. وهم قوله : (أو أنَّ المراد ... إلخ) : تنويع في الرد على من يقول بالقدم، الفلاسفة . وحاصل مذهب الفلاسفة: أنَّ الحادث عـنـدهـم قـسـمـان: حادث بالذات، ويفسرونه بما يحتاج في وجوده إلى مؤثر، سواء سبقه عدم أو لا، فالأول : كأفراد الإنسان، والثَّاني : كالأفلاك؛ فإنَّها محتاجة في وجودها للمؤثر ولم يسبقها عدم، وحادث بالزَّمان، ويفسرونه بما سبق وجوده عدم؛ كأفراد الإنسان والقديم قسمان: قديم بالذات، وهو ما لا يحتاج في وجوده لمؤثر؛ كذات المولى تعالى، وقديم بالزمان، وهو ما لا يسبقه عدم، واحتاج في وجوده لمؤثّر ؛ كالأفلاك فإنَّها عندهم لم يسبقها عدم؛ لأنَّها ناشئة عن العقول بطريق العلة ويقولون : إنَّ واجب الوجود الله واحد من كل جهة، فلا قدرة له ولا إرادة، ولا صفة له زائدة على الذات والواحد من كلِّ جهة إنَّما ينشأ عنه واحد بطريق العلة، فالواحد الذي ينشأ عنه يقال له : العقل الأوَّل، ثمَّ إِنَّ ذلك العقل متّصف بالإمكان من حيث إنَّ الغير أثر فيه، وبالوجوب فهو قديم لعلَّته، حادث باعتبار ذاته، فنشأ عنه باعتبار الجهة الأولى عقل ثان، ونشأ عنه من الجهة الثَّانية فلك أوَّل، وهو المسمى في لسان الشرع بـ(العرش). ثمَّ إِنَّ هذا العقل الثَّاني متّصف بالإمكان من حيث إنَّ الغير أثر فيه، وبالوجوب لعلَّته فهو حادث لذاته، قديم لعلَّته، فنشأ عنه باعتبار الجهة الأولى فلك ثان، وهو المسمى في لسان الشَّرع بـ(الكرسي)، وباعتبار الجهة الثانية عقل ثالث مدبّر لذلك الفلك الثَّاني . ثمَّ إِنَّ ذلك العقل الثَّالث متّصف بالإمكان من حيث إنَّ الغير أثر فيه، وبالوجوب من حيث علّته، فنشأ عنه من الجهة الأولى فلك ثالث، وهو المسمَّى بـ( السَّماء السَّابعة)، ونشأ عنه من الجهة الثَّانية عقل رابع مدبّر لذلك الفلك الثَّالث ، وهكذا إلى سماء الدُّنيا، فتكاملت الأفلاك تسعة والعقول عشرة . ويسمون العقل المدبّر لفلك القمر، وهو سماء الدُّنيا بـ(العقل الفيَّاض) ؛ لإفاضته على ما تحت فلك القمر من أنواع الحيوانات والنباتات والمعادن، وبهذا ظهر لك وجه قولهم : إنَّ الأفلاك حادثة بالذات، قديمة بالزَّمان، وأنَّه لا أوّل لها تبعاً لعلَّتها ؛ لأنَّ المعلول يقارن علته، ومثلها في ذلك العقول وسائر الأنواع من الحيوانات والنباتات والمعادن، وأما أفراد تلك الأنواع؛ فهي حادثة ذاتاً وزماناً. انتهى. الله ومذهب أهل السُّنَّة : أنَّ القديم هو القديم بالذات لا غير، وهو تعالى وصفاته، وأنَّ الحادث هو الحادث بالذات لا غير، وهو ما سوى الله تعالى وما قالته الفلاسفة أوهام وخيالات وكفر
The origination of the world. Or that the meaning: that it must have temporal origination just as its originator must have eternity, so it is not objected that the philosopher does not affirm its origination. And [this is] an illusion. His saying: (Or that the meaning ... etc.): a variation in refuting those who affirm eternity, the philosophers. The summary of the philosophers' doctrine: that the originated according to them are two kinds: originated in essence (ḥādith bi al-dhāt), which they interpret as what needs an effect in its existence, whether preceded by non-existence or not. The first: like individual humans, and the second: like the celestial spheres; for they need an effect in their existence but non-existence did not precede them. And originated in time (ḥādith bi al-zamān), which they interpret as what is preceded in existence by non-existence; like individual humans. And the eternal is two kinds: eternal in essence (qadīm bi al-dhāt), which is what does not need an effect in its existence; like the essence of the Lord Most High. And eternal in time (qadīm bi al-zamān), which is what non-existence does not precede, but it needs an effect in its existence; like the celestial spheres, for according to them non-existence did not precede them, because they arise from the intellects by way of causality. And they say: that the Necessary Existent, God, is one from every aspect, so He has no power nor will, nor any attribute additional to the essence. And the one from every aspect only produces one by way of causality. So the one that arises from Him is called the First Intellect (al-ʿaql al-awwal). Then that Intellect is characterized by contingency inasmuch as the other has an effect in it, and by necessity inasmuch as it is eternal by its cause, originated with respect to its essence. So from it arises from the first aspect a second intellect, and from the second aspect a first sphere, which is called in the language of the Law the Throne (al-ʿarsh). Then this second intellect is characterized by contingency inasmuch as the other has an effect in it, and by necessity by its cause, so it is originated in itself, eternal by its cause. So from it arises from the first aspect a second sphere, which is called in the language of the Law the Footstool (al-kursī), and from the second aspect a third intellect governing that second sphere. Then that third intellect is characterized by contingency inasmuch as the other has an effect in it, and by necessity inasmuch as its cause, so from it arises from the first aspect a third sphere, which is called the Seventh Heaven (al-samāʾ al-sābiʿa), and from the second aspect a fourth intellect governing that third sphere, and so on up to the heaven of this world, thus the spheres became complete as nine and the intellects as ten. And they call the intellect governing the sphere of the moon, which is the heaven of this world, the Flowing Intellect (al-ʿaql al-fayyāḍ), because of its flowing upon what is beneath the sphere of the moon of the kinds of animals, plants and minerals. And by this it became clear to you the meaning of their saying: that the spheres are originated in essence, eternal in time, and that they have no beginning following their cause, because the effect is concomitant with its cause. And similar to them in that are the intellects and the rest of the kinds of animals, plants and minerals. As for individuals of those kinds, they are originated in essence and time. End. God. And the doctrine of the Ahl al-Sunna: that the eternal is the eternal in essence only, and He is the Most High and His attributes, and that the originated is the originated in essence only, and it is whatever is besides God Most High. And what the philosophers said are illusions, fantasies and disbelief.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed exposition of the philosophers' (falāsifa) classification of eternity and temporal origination, along with their emanationist cosmology, followed by the contrasting Sunni position. The structure is as follows:

The discussion begins by clarifying a point of refutation: the intended meaning is that the world must have temporal origination just as its Creator must be eternal, so the philosopher's denial of its origination is not a valid objection. The phrase 'وهم' (illusion) signals that the philosophers' claim is baseless.

Then the author summarizes the philosophers' doctrine. According to them, the 'originated' (ḥādith) is divided into two types:
1. Originated in essence (ḥādith bi al-dhāt): something that needs an efficient cause for its existence, whether or not it was preceded by non-existence. Examples: individual humans (preceded by non-existence) and the celestial spheres (not preceded by non-existence).
2. Originated in time (ḥādith bi al-zamān): something whose existence is preceded by non-existence; e.g., individual humans.

Similarly, the 'eternal' (qadīm) is divided into:
1. Eternal in essence (qadīm bi al-dhāt): something that needs no cause for its existence; only the essence of God Most High.
2. Eternal in time (qadīm bi al-zamān): something not preceded by non-existence but still requiring a cause; e.g., the celestial spheres, which according to the philosophers arise from the intellects by way of causality and therefore have no temporal beginning.

Next, the author explains the philosophers' emanation scheme. They hold that the Necessary Existent (God) is absolutely one, having no power, will, or attributes distinct from the essence. From such a simple unity only one thing can proceed. That first emanation is called the First Intellect (al-ʿaql al-awwal). This intellect is characterized by both contingency (imkān) because it is produced by another, and necessity (wujūb) because it is eternal by its cause. From this intellect, in one aspect, proceeds a second intellect; and in another aspect, proceeds the first sphere, which in religious language is called the Throne (al-ʿarsh). Then from the second intellect, in one aspect, proceeds a second sphere (the Footstool, al-kursī), and in another aspect, a third intellect. This cascading process continues until nine celestial spheres and ten intellects are complete. The tenth intellect, governing the sphere of the moon (the lowest heaven), is called the Flowing Intellect (al-ʿaql al-fayyāḍ) because it emanates forms onto the sublunary world of animals, plants, and minerals.

Thus, the spheres are 'originated in essence' because they depend on a cause, but 'eternal in time' because they have no beginning—they are concomitant with their cause. The same applies to the intellects and to the species of sublunary things. Only individual members of those species are originated in both sense and time.

After concluding the exposition with 'انتهى' (end), the text presents the Sunni position: the only eternal is He who is eternal in essence, namely God and His attributes. Everything else is originated in essence, with no distinction between essential and temporal origination. Therefore, the philosophers' elaborate classifications and emanation doctrine are dismissed as illusions, fantasies, and disbelief.

حادث بالزمان
قديم بالذات
قديم بالزمان
الإمكان
الوجوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the philosophers' 'eternal in time' means something can be both eternal and caused, which Sunni theology denies.
Correction: The philosophers' 'eternal in time' is not true eternity (which requires no cause) but rather temporal perpetuity combined with causal dependence. Sunnis reject any such classification, affirming only God as eternal.

Checkpoint
According to the philosophers, which of the following is an example of something that is originated in essence but not preceded by non-existence?
A) Individual humans
B) The celestial spheres
C) The essence of God
D) Minerals

Key Takeaway
The philosophers distinguish two forms of origination (essential and temporal) and two forms of eternity (essential and temporal), with the celestial spheres being a key example of something that is originated in essence yet eternal in time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as if your own existence is merely 'originated in time'—a one-time event in the past—or do you recognize your constant need for the Creator's sustaining power every moment, as the philosophers admitted even for the celestial spheres? How will you remind yourself of this essential dependence today?
?
If the celestial spheres, which are vast and seemingly permanent, still require a cause for their existence, what does that say about the things you rely on for security—your health, wealth, or relationships? Are you treating any of these as if they were 'eternal in essence'? What one step can you take to redirect that trust?
?
The philosophers distinguished between 'originated in essence' and 'originated in time.' Which category describes your current awareness of your need for Allah: do you only turn to Him when you face a temporal lack, or do you acknowledge that your very essence is dependent on Him at every instant? What will you do to cultivate the latter state of heart?

8 min
The Emanation of the Intellects and Spheres
Al-Sawi details the emanation of ten intellects and nine spheres from the First Intellect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' emanation theory, including the generation of ten intellects and nine celestial spheres from the First Intellect, culminating in the Flowing Intellect (al-ʿaql al-fayyāḍ).

Core Idea
From the absolutely simple One proceeds only one; from that one proceeds a cascade of intellects and spheres.

Having established the fourfold classification, al-Sawi now explains the philosophers' detailed cosmology of emanation (ṣudūr). This theory posits a series of intellectual celestial beings (intellects) and spheres that arise from the First Intellect by a process of necessary causation. The passage traces the emanation step by step, showing how each intellect gives rise to a lower intellect and a sphere, until the material world is reached.

Guided Path
1
Read the emanation chain step by step
Follow the sequence from the First Intellect to the tenth intellect. Notice how each level involves contingency and necessity.
The process is deterministic in their view.
2
Identify the role of the Flowing Intellect
The tenth intellect governs the sublunary world. Note its name and function.
3
Understand the conclusion about spheres
The passage ends by explaining why the spheres are originated in essence but eternal in time.
This ties back to the classification in lesson 1.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the emanation process is voluntary creation, but the philosophers see it as necessary causation.
Correction: The passage emphasizes that the First Intellect arises from God 'by way of causality' (bi ṭarīq al-ʿilla), not by free choice, and each subsequent emanation is a necessary consequence of the preceding intellect's nature.

Checkpoint
According to the emanation theory, what arises from the second aspect of the First Intellect?
A) The Second Intellect
B) The First Sphere (Throne)
C) The Flowing Intellect

The philosophers' emanation theory explains the existence of the celestial spheres as necessary, eternal in time but dependent in essence, arising from a chain of intellects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The philosophers claim that from the absolutely simple One, only one thing can proceed. How does this constrain your concept of God's creativity? Does this align with or challenge your belief in a God who directly creates everything by will and power? What does this imply for your understanding of divine freedom?
?
In this emanation scheme, the First Intellect is both contingent and necessary. Do you see any aspect of your own existence as similarly dual—dependent on God yet having a sense of autonomous self? How does this distinction between essential and temporal origination affect how you view your own relationship to God as Creator?
?
The passage states that the spheres and intellects are eternal in time but originated in essence. Does this notion of 'dependent eternity' resonate with you? How does it compare to Islamic creed that everything besides God is temporally created? What might be at stake in this difference for your daily reliance on God?

The Sunni Response: Only God is Eternal
Al-Sawi states the Sunni position on eternity and origins, rejecting the philosophers' classification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni theological position that rejects the philosophers' classification and affirms that only God and His attributes are eternal, and everything else is originated.

Core Idea
Sunnis reject any division of eternity or origination; only God is eternal in essence, everything else is originated.

After presenting the complex and multi-tiered system of the philosophers, al-Sawi cuts through it with the simple, definitive statement of Sunni orthodoxy. The eternal (qadīm) is only that which is eternal in essence—God and His attributes. The originated (ḥādith) is everything besides God, with no subdivision by time or essence. The philosophers' elaborate scheme is dismissed as illusions and disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the Sunni doctrine statement
Notice the absolute binary: eternal = God and His attributes; originated = everything else.
2
Contrast with philosophers' four categories
Compare this simple division to the philosophers' four categories. What is the key difference?
3
Understand the dismissal
The passage ends by calling the philosophers' ideas 'illusions, fantasies, and disbelief.' Reflect on why such strong language is used.

حدوث العالم أو أنَّ المراد : أَنَّه يجب له الحدوث كما يجب لمُحدِثه القِدَم، فلا يرد أنَّ حدوثه لا يقول به الفلسفي. وهم قوله : (أو أنَّ المراد ... إلخ) : تنويع في الرد على من يقول بالقدم، الفلاسفة . وحاصل مذهب الفلاسفة: أنَّ الحادث عـنـدهـم قـسـمـان: حادث بالذات، ويفسرونه بما يحتاج في وجوده إلى مؤثر، سواء سبقه عدم أو لا، فالأول : كأفراد الإنسان، والثَّاني : كالأفلاك؛ فإنَّها محتاجة في وجودها للمؤثر ولم يسبقها عدم، وحادث بالزَّمان، ويفسرونه بما سبق وجوده عدم؛ كأفراد الإنسان والقديم قسمان: قديم بالذات، وهو ما لا يحتاج في وجوده لمؤثر؛ كذات المولى تعالى، وقديم بالزمان، وهو ما لا يسبقه عدم، واحتاج في وجوده لمؤثّر ؛ كالأفلاك فإنَّها عندهم لم يسبقها عدم؛ لأنَّها ناشئة عن العقول بطريق العلة ويقولون : إنَّ واجب الوجود الله واحد من كل جهة، فلا قدرة له ولا إرادة، ولا صفة له زائدة على الذات والواحد من كلِّ جهة إنَّما ينشأ عنه واحد بطريق العلة، فالواحد الذي ينشأ عنه يقال له : العقل الأوَّل، ثمَّ إِنَّ ذلك العقل متّصف بالإمكان من حيث إنَّ الغير أثر فيه، وبالوجوب فهو قديم لعلَّته، حادث باعتبار ذاته، فنشأ عنه باعتبار الجهة الأولى عقل ثان، ونشأ عنه من الجهة الثَّانية فلك أوَّل، وهو المسمى في لسان الشرع بـ(العرش). ثمَّ إِنَّ هذا العقل الثَّاني متّصف بالإمكان من حيث إنَّ الغير أثر فيه، وبالوجوب لعلَّته فهو حادث لذاته، قديم لعلَّته، فنشأ عنه باعتبار الجهة الأولى فلك ثان، وهو المسمى في لسان الشَّرع بـ(الكرسي)، وباعتبار الجهة الثانية عقل ثالث مدبّر لذلك الفلك الثَّاني . ثمَّ إِنَّ ذلك العقل الثَّالث متّصف بالإمكان من حيث إنَّ الغير أثر فيه، وبالوجوب من حيث علّته، فنشأ عنه من الجهة الأولى فلك ثالث، وهو المسمَّى بـ( السَّماء السَّابعة)، ونشأ عنه من الجهة الثَّانية عقل رابع مدبّر لذلك الفلك الثَّالث ، وهكذا إلى سماء الدُّنيا، فتكاملت الأفلاك تسعة والعقول عشرة . ويسمون العقل المدبّر لفلك القمر، وهو سماء الدُّنيا بـ(العقل الفيَّاض) ؛ لإفاضته على ما تحت فلك القمر من أنواع الحيوانات والنباتات والمعادن، وبهذا ظهر لك وجه قولهم : إنَّ الأفلاك حادثة بالذات، قديمة بالزَّمان، وأنَّه لا أوّل لها تبعاً لعلَّتها ؛ لأنَّ المعلول يقارن علته، ومثلها في ذلك العقول وسائر الأنواع من الحيوانات والنباتات والمعادن، وأما أفراد تلك الأنواع؛ فهي حادثة ذاتاً وزماناً. انتهى. الله ومذهب أهل السُّنَّة : أنَّ القديم هو القديم بالذات لا غير، وهو تعالى وصفاته، وأنَّ الحادث هو الحادث بالذات لا غير، وهو ما سوى الله تعالى وما قالته الفلاسفة أوهام وخيالات وكفر
The origination of the world. Or that the meaning: that it must have temporal origination just as its originator must have eternity, so it is not objected that the philosopher does not affirm its origination. And [this is] an illusion. His saying: (Or that the meaning ... etc.): a variation in refuting those who affirm eternity, the philosophers. The summary of the philosophers' doctrine: that the originated according to them are two kinds: originated in essence (ḥādith bi al-dhāt), which they interpret as what needs an effect in its existence, whether preceded by non-existence or not. The first: like individual humans, and the second: like the celestial spheres; for they need an effect in their existence but non-existence did not precede them. And originated in time (ḥādith bi al-zamān), which they interpret as what is preceded in existence by non-existence; like individual humans. And the eternal is two kinds: eternal in essence (qadīm bi al-dhāt), which is what does not need an effect in its existence; like the essence of the Lord Most High. And eternal in time (qadīm bi al-zamān), which is what non-existence does not precede, but it needs an effect in its existence; like the celestial spheres, for according to them non-existence did not precede them, because they arise from the intellects by way of causality. And they say: that the Necessary Existent, God, is one from every aspect, so He has no power nor will, nor any attribute additional to the essence. And the one from every aspect only produces one by way of causality. So the one that arises from Him is called the First Intellect (al-ʿaql al-awwal). Then that Intellect is characterized by contingency inasmuch as the other has an effect in it, and by necessity inasmuch as it is eternal by its cause, originated with respect to its essence. So from it arises from the first aspect a second intellect, and from the second aspect a first sphere, which is called in the language of the Law the Throne (al-ʿarsh). Then this second intellect is characterized by contingency inasmuch as the other has an effect in it, and by necessity by its cause, so it is originated in itself, eternal by its cause. So from it arises from the first aspect a second sphere, which is called in the language of the Law the Footstool (al-kursī), and from the second aspect a third intellect governing that second sphere. Then that third intellect is characterized by contingency inasmuch as the other has an effect in it, and by necessity inasmuch as its cause, so from it arises from the first aspect a third sphere, which is called the Seventh Heaven (al-samāʾ al-sābiʿa), and from the second aspect a fourth intellect governing that third sphere, and so on up to the heaven of this world, thus the spheres became complete as nine and the intellects as ten. And they call the intellect governing the sphere of the moon, which is the heaven of this world, the Flowing Intellect (al-ʿaql al-fayyāḍ), because of its flowing upon what is beneath the sphere of the moon of the kinds of animals, plants and minerals. And by this it became clear to you the meaning of their saying: that the spheres are originated in essence, eternal in time, and that they have no beginning following their cause, because the effect is concomitant with its cause. And similar to them in that are the intellects and the rest of the kinds of animals, plants and minerals. As for individuals of those kinds, they are originated in essence and time. End. God. And the doctrine of the Ahl al-Sunna: that the eternal is the eternal in essence only, and He is the Most High and His attributes, and that the originated is the originated in essence only, and it is whatever is besides God Most High. And what the philosophers said are illusions, fantasies and disbelief.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed exposition of the philosophers' (falāsifa) classification of eternity and temporal origination, along with their emanationist cosmology, followed by the contrasting Sunni position. The structure is as follows:

The discussion begins by clarifying a point of refutation: the intended meaning is that the world must have temporal origination just as its Creator must be eternal, so the philosopher's denial of its origination is not a valid objection. The phrase 'وهم' (illusion) signals that the philosophers' claim is baseless.

Then the author summarizes the philosophers' doctrine. According to them, the 'originated' (ḥādith) is divided into two types:
1. Originated in essence (ḥādith bi al-dhāt): something that needs an efficient cause for its existence, whether or not it was preceded by non-existence. Examples: individual humans (preceded by non-existence) and the celestial spheres (not preceded by non-existence).
2. Originated in time (ḥādith bi al-zamān): something whose existence is preceded by non-existence; e.g., individual humans.

Similarly, the 'eternal' (qadīm) is divided into:
1. Eternal in essence (qadīm bi al-dhāt): something that needs no cause for its existence; only the essence of God Most High.
2. Eternal in time (qadīm bi al-zamān): something not preceded by non-existence but still requiring a cause; e.g., the celestial spheres, which according to the philosophers arise from the intellects by way of causality and therefore have no temporal beginning.

Next, the author explains the philosophers' emanation scheme. They hold that the Necessary Existent (God) is absolutely one, having no power, will, or attributes distinct from the essence. From such a simple unity only one thing can proceed. That first emanation is called the First Intellect (al-ʿaql al-awwal). This intellect is characterized by both contingency (imkān) because it is produced by another, and necessity (wujūb) because it is eternal by its cause. From this intellect, in one aspect, proceeds a second intellect; and in another aspect, proceeds the first sphere, which in religious language is called the Throne (al-ʿarsh). Then from the second intellect, in one aspect, proceeds a second sphere (the Footstool, al-kursī), and in another aspect, a third intellect. This cascading process continues until nine celestial spheres and ten intellects are complete. The tenth intellect, governing the sphere of the moon (the lowest heaven), is called the Flowing Intellect (al-ʿaql al-fayyāḍ) because it emanates forms onto the sublunary world of animals, plants, and minerals.

Thus, the spheres are 'originated in essence' because they depend on a cause, but 'eternal in time' because they have no beginning—they are concomitant with their cause. The same applies to the intellects and to the species of sublunary things. Only individual members of those species are originated in both sense and time.

After concluding the exposition with 'انتهى' (end), the text presents the Sunni position: the only eternal is He who is eternal in essence, namely God and His attributes. Everything else is originated in essence, with no distinction between essential and temporal origination. Therefore, the philosophers' elaborate classifications and emanation doctrine are dismissed as illusions, fantasies, and disbelief.

Key Terms
قديم بالذات
الحادث
أهل السنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the philosophers' classification could be reconciled with Sunni theology.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that what the philosophers said are illusions and disbelief, so there is no reconciliation.

Checkpoint
According to the Sunni doctrine presented here, which of the following is considered eternal (qadīm)?
A) The celestial spheres
B) God and His attributes
C) The First Intellect
D) Everything besides God

Key Takeaway
Sunnis affirm a strict binary: only God and His attributes are eternal; everything else is originated, and any other classification is rejected.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read that only God is eternal in essence. Is there anything in your life—a career, a relationship, an ambition—that you treat as if it will last forever? How can you reorient your heart to see it as originated and temporary?
?
The philosophers used rational arguments to divide eternity into categories. In what area of your life do you use rationalizations to justify something that contradicts clear revelation? Will you submit to Allah's words or cling to your own logic?
?
Al-Sawi calls the philosophers' ideas 'illusions, fantasies, and disbelief.' When you read that, do you feel a defensive reaction or humble acceptance? What does your reaction reveal about your attachment to your own intellect over Allah's truth?

The Seven Demands and the First: Proving an Extra Substance
Explains the first demand of the seven: proving an extra substance on bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the first demand aims to prove an additional entity (accidents) upon bodies to establish their temporal origination from observation.

Core Idea
The first demand shows that bodies must have accidents, proving their contingency.

The scholars formulated seven demands to refute the philosophers' claim of the world's pre-eternity. These are summarized in a verse of rajaz. In this lesson, we examine the first demand, which seeks to prove an entity extra to bodies (accidents) by direct observation, thereby setting the stage for arguing that bodies are temporally originated.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the seven demands are compressed into a poetic line.
2
Focus on the first demand (زيد)
Understand that 'زيد' refers to proving an additional entity (al-zā'id) on bodies. This is the first demand.
The proof is observation (mushāhada).
3
Examine the dialectical argument
The author includes a dialogue: if the philosophers deny any dispute, they are refuted; if they admit it, they prove the existence of the extra entity.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself why proving an extra substance is important for establishing the temporality of bodies.
This connects to the overall goal of refuting the philosophers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر العلماء مطالب سبعة قصدوا بها الرد على الفلاسفة أيضاً، جمعها بعضهم في قوله من الرجز: زيد م قام ما انتقل ما كمنى ما انفك لا عدم قديم لحانا

فقوله: (زيد) إشارة لإثبات زائد على الأجرام، حتى يصح الاستدلال به على حدوث الأجرام، ودليل ذلك المشاهدة. قال بعضهم: يقال لهم: نزاعكم معنا موجود أولا، فإن قالوا: لا، كفونا المؤنة، وإلا؛ فقد أثبتوا الزائد. وقوله: (م قام بحذف ألف ما للوزن) إشارة لقولهم: لا نسلم عدم الأعراض لجواز أن الحركة تقوم بنفسها إذا سكن الجسم مثلا. ورده: أن العرض لا يقوم بنفسه، إذ لا تعقل صفة من غير موصوف، ولا حركة بدون متحرك...إلى غير ذلك. وقوله: (ما انتقل بسكون اللام) لرد قولهم: لا نسلم عدم الأعراض حتى ينتج حدوثها؛ لجواز أن الساكن إذا تحرك انتقل السكون لمحل آخر.
And the scholars mentioned seven demands, intending thereby also to refute the philosophers. Some of them collected them in his saying in rajaz: 'Increased, stood, did not transfer, what we hid, did not cease, no non-existence, a pre-eternal appeared to us.' So his saying: (Increased) refers to proving an additional [entity] upon bodies, so that inference by it to the temporal origination of bodies is valid, and its proof is observation. Some said: One says to them: Your dispute with us exists first; if they say no, they have spared us the trouble; otherwise, they have proven the additional. And his saying: (Stood) with the alif of 'ma' dropped for meter, refers to their saying: We do not concede the non-existence of accidents because it is possible that motion subsists in itself when the body becomes still, for example. And its refutation: that an accident does not subsist in itself, for an attribute without a possessor is inconceivable, nor motion without a moving thing...etc. And his saying: (Did not transfer) with the lam silent, to refute their saying: We do not concede the non-existence of accidents such that their temporality follows, because it is possible that when the still thing moves, rest transfers to another locus.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage introduces seven demands (مطالب) used by scholars to refute the philosophers' arguments for the pre-eternity of the world. The demands are summarized in a line of rajaz poetry, and the passage explains the first three. The first demand (زيد) is to prove an entity additional to bodies (i.e., accidents) to then argue for their temporality based on observable change. The second demand (م قام) refutes the philosophers' claim that accidents like motion can subsist in themselves without a body; the refutation is that an accident cannot subsist independently because every attribute requires a subject. The third demand (ما انتقل) refutes the claim that when a body moves, its previous state of rest transfers to another body; such transfer is impossible because rest is an accident attached to the original body. Each demand serves to establish the temporal nature of bodies by showing the contingency of accidents.

Key Terms
مطالب سبعة
زائد على الأجرام
مشاهدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The first demand is about proving that bodies are themselves accidents.
Correction: The demand is not that bodies are accidents, but that there is an additional entity (accidents) upon bodies.

Checkpoint
What does the demand 'زيد' aim to prove?
A) That motion can subsist in itself
B) An additional entity beyond bodies to infer their temporality
C) That rest transfers between bodies
D) That bodies are pre-eternal

Key Takeaway
The first demand establishes that bodies possess accidents through observable change, serving as evidence for their temporality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe your own body changing—aging, illness, or even your moods shifting—do you see these changes as a reminder that you are not self-sufficient but utterly dependent on Allah? Or do you take them for granted?
?
The dialectical argument shows that even those who deny accidents implicitly affirm them by the act of disputing. In your own life, are there aspects of faith that you deny with your words but affirm with your actions (e.g., acting as if this world is permanent while claiming to believe in the Hereafter)?
?
The scholars used observation to prove an unseen reality about bodies. When you witness the constant changes in the world, does it stir in you a conviction that a Creator governs all? Or are you distracted from that truth? What will you do today to consciously reflect on a single change in nature as a sign of Allah?

The Second Demand: Accidents Cannot Subsist by Themselves
Refutes the philosophers' argument that accidents can subsist without a body.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the second demand refutes the philosophers' claim that accidents like motion can exist independently of a body.

Core Idea
Accidents cannot subsist in themselves; every attribute requires a subject.

The second demand targets the philosophers' objection that accidents might not be dependent on bodies. The scholars argue that an accident is inconceivable without a subject—no motion without a moving thing—thus upholding the necessary connection between accidents and bodies.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for the second demand
Read the Arabic passage and translation carefully. Note that the word 'قام' in the verse refers to this demand.
The meter requires dropping the alif of 'ما', so it appears as 'م قام'.
2
Identify the philosophers' claim
The philosophers claim that the non-existence of accidents is not conceded because motion could subsist in itself when a body becomes still.
They use the example of motion persisting after a body stops.
3
Understand the refutation
The scholars refute by stating that an accident does not subsist in itself; an attribute cannot exist without a possessor, nor motion without a moving thing.
This is a fundamental principle of kalam.
4
Connect to the overall argument
Realize that this refutation strengthens the case that accidents are contingent upon bodies, leading to the temporality of bodies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

What is the refutation of the philosophers' claim about motion subsisting in itself?
A) Motion is eternal

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You just learned that an accident cannot subsist without a subject. Now think about your own anger: does it exist without you? When you are angry, who is angry? If you were not present, could anger remain? This lesson forces you to see that all your attributes depend on your existence. So who is the ultimate source of your existence? How does this realization change the way you view your own self? Commit today to remembering that every quality you have points back to the One who gave you existence.
?
The philosophers claimed motion could subsist without a moving thing. In your life, do you ever act as if your habits or personality traits have a life of their own—as if they exist independently of your choices? How does this lesson challenge that assumption? Will you today take ownership of your actions and see them as expressions of your very being, not as separate forces?

The Third Demand: The Impossibility of Transferring Rest
Refutes the possibility of rest transferring between bodies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the third demand refutes the idea that rest can transfer when a body moves, thereby reinforcing the temporality of accidents.

Core Idea
Rest, as an accident, cannot transfer from one body to another.

The third demand addresses another philosophical objection: when a stationary body moves, its rest might transfer to another locus. The scholars reject this as impossible because rest is an accident inherent to the original body, not a substance that can move.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for the third demand
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note that 'ما انتقل' in the verse refers to this demand.
The lam is silent for meter.
2
Identify the philosophers' position
The philosophers say that the non-existence of accidents is not conceded because rest could transfer when a body moves.
This would imply accidents do not necessarily cease to exist.
3
Understand the refutation
The refutation is that rest is an accident attached to a specific body; transfer is impossible.
Accidents cannot migrate.
4
Relate to the overall argument
This shows that accidents are not enduring; they come and go, proving the temporality of bodies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر العلماء مطالب سبعة قصدوا بها الرد على الفلاسفة أيضاً، جمعها بعضهم في قوله من الرجز: زيد م قام ما انتقل ما كمنى ما انفك لا عدم قديم لحانا

فقوله: (زيد) إشارة لإثبات زائد على الأجرام، حتى يصح الاستدلال به على حدوث الأجرام، ودليل ذلك المشاهدة. قال بعضهم: يقال لهم: نزاعكم معنا موجود أولا، فإن قالوا: لا، كفونا المؤنة، وإلا؛ فقد أثبتوا الزائد. وقوله: (م قام بحذف ألف ما للوزن) إشارة لقولهم: لا نسلم عدم الأعراض لجواز أن الحركة تقوم بنفسها إذا سكن الجسم مثلا. ورده: أن العرض لا يقوم بنفسه، إذ لا تعقل صفة من غير موصوف، ولا حركة بدون متحرك...إلى غير ذلك. وقوله: (ما انتقل بسكون اللام) لرد قولهم: لا نسلم عدم الأعراض حتى ينتج حدوثها؛ لجواز أن الساكن إذا تحرك انتقل السكون لمحل آخر.
And the scholars mentioned seven demands, intending thereby also to refute the philosophers. Some of them collected them in his saying in rajaz: 'Increased, stood, did not transfer, what we hid, did not cease, no non-existence, a pre-eternal appeared to us.' So his saying: (Increased) refers to proving an additional [entity] upon bodies, so that inference by it to the temporal origination of bodies is valid, and its proof is observation. Some said: One says to them: Your dispute with us exists first; if they say no, they have spared us the trouble; otherwise, they have proven the additional. And his saying: (Stood) with the alif of 'ma' dropped for meter, refers to their saying: We do not concede the non-existence of accidents because it is possible that motion subsists in itself when the body becomes still, for example. And its refutation: that an accident does not subsist in itself, for an attribute without a possessor is inconceivable, nor motion without a moving thing...etc. And his saying: (Did not transfer) with the lam silent, to refute their saying: We do not concede the non-existence of accidents such that their temporality follows, because it is possible that when the still thing moves, rest transfers to another locus.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage introduces seven demands (مطالب) used by scholars to refute the philosophers' arguments for the pre-eternity of the world. The demands are summarized in a line of rajaz poetry, and the passage explains the first three. The first demand (زيد) is to prove an entity additional to bodies (i.e., accidents) to then argue for their temporality based on observable change. The second demand (م قام) refutes the philosophers' claim that accidents like motion can subsist in themselves without a body; the refutation is that an accident cannot subsist independently because every attribute requires a subject. The third demand (ما انتقل) refutes the claim that when a body moves, its previous state of rest transfers to another body; such transfer is impossible because rest is an accident attached to the original body. Each demand serves to establish the temporal nature of bodies by showing the contingency of accidents.

Key Terms
ما انتقل
سكون
انتقال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Rest is a substance that can move between bodies.
Correction: Rest is an accident and cannot transfer; it exists only in its original subject.

Checkpoint
What does the third demand ('ما انتقل') refute?
A) That rest can transfer to another body
B) That motion is eternal
C) That bodies are created
D) That accidents are impossible

Key Takeaway
The third demand shows that rest, as an accident, cannot transfer, thus accidents are dependent on bodies and temporal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If rest cannot transfer or persist, then your very stillness at this moment is entirely dependent on Allah's continuous creation. When you are still, do you recognize that your existence is being upheld moment by moment? How will you cultivate this awareness in your daily life?
?
The philosophers assumed that rest could be transferred, betraying a reliance on independent persistence. In what areas of your life do you mistakenly think your spiritual state—faith, repentance, or good deeds—can be 'stored' or transferred to cover future shortcomings? What commitment can you make today to renew your reliance on Allah each moment?

Refuting Jabriyya and Qadariyya
Sanusi refutes both sects and gives their rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari position refutes both the Jabriyya (extreme predestinarianism) and the Qadariyya (free-will sect), and why one is ruled disbelief while the other is not.

Core Idea
The difference between voluntary and involuntary action is self-evident; both absolute compulsion and absolute free will are false.

Sanusi tackles two opposite heresies: the Jabriyya who deny human power entirely, and the Qadariyya who give human power an independent role. He begins with an obvious premise—the difference between voluntary and involuntary motion—and then states the rulings on each sect. This passage also addresses a key objection from the Qadariyya about divine justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how the author contrasts the two sects.
2
Identify the two sects and their claims
Find the descriptions of Jabriyya and Qadariyya. What does each claim about human power and actions?
Jabriyya compare humans to a thread in the wind.
3
Understand the rulings and the objection
Why are Jabriyya definitely disbelievers? Why is there disagreement about Qadariyya? How does the author respond to the Qadariyya's objection about divine justice?
The key is the concept of 'acquisition' (kasb).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والفرق بين الحركة الاختيارية والاضطرارية مما هو بديهي عند عاقل . كُلِّ فبطل قولُ الجبرية بأنه لا قدرة للعبد تقارن فعلاً له أصلاً، بل هو مجبور ظاهراً وباطناً كالخيط المعلَّق في الهواء، تميله الرِّياح بلا اختيار له في شيء أصلاً، وقولُ القدرية بتأثير القدرة الحادثة في الأفعال على طبق إرادة العبد. والجبرية كفارٌ قطعاً ؛ لأنَّ مذهبهم ينفي التكليف الذي جاء به الرُّسُل عليهم السَّلام، وفي كفر القدرية خلاف، الأصح عدم كفرهم؛ وإن لزمهم إثبات الشَّريك الله تعالى، إلا أنَّهم لما أثبتوا الله تعالى خَلْقَ العبد وقدرته وإرادته، صار فعل العبد في الحقيقة مخلوقاً له تعالى قوله : (فبطل قول الجبريَّة) : بسكون الباء وفتحها. وقوله : (وقول القدريَّة) : بالرَّفع معطوف على (قول الجبريَّة). قوله : (بتأثير القدرة الحادثة في الأفعال . . . إلخ) : أي : وبنوا على ذلك أموراً فاسدة باطلة؛ منها : أنَّهم قالوا : لو كانت هذه الأفعال مخلوقة الله كما تقولون لكان تعذيب الله له ظلماً . قلنا : التَّعذيب بالنظر للجزء الاختياري، وهو الكي
And the difference between voluntary and involuntary motion is something obvious to every rational person. So the statement of the Jabriyya is nullified – that there is no power for the servant concurrent with any act of his at all, rather he is compelled outwardly and inwardly like a thread suspended in the air, the winds tilt it without any choice for him in anything at all – and the statement of the Qadariyya – that the originated power has influence in the acts according to the will of the servant. And the Jabriyya are disbelievers definitely, because their doctrine negates the obligation which the messengers (peace be upon them) brought. And regarding the disbelief of the Qadariyya there is disagreement; the correct view is that they are not disbelievers, even though they necessitate affirming a partner with Allah (may He be exalted), except that when they affirmed that Allah (may He be exalted) created the servant, his power and his will, the act of the servant becomes in reality created by Him (may He be exalted). His statement: 'So the statement of the Jabriyya is nullified' – with sukoon on the bā' or with fatḥa. And his statement: 'and the statement of the Qadariyya' – with raf' coordinated with 'statement of the Jabriyya'. His statement: 'that the originated power has influence in the acts etc.' – meaning: they built upon that corrupt, false matters; among them: they said: 'If these acts were created by Allah as you say, then Allah's punishing him would be injustice.' We said: 'The punishment is with respect to the voluntary component, which is the acquisition[?]'
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of two extreme sects. First, it establishes that the difference between voluntary and involuntary motion is immediately obvious to any rational person. This serves as a premise to reject both extremes. The Jabriyya claim that the servant has no power at all, being like a thread in the wind. The Qadariyya claim that human power actually creates actions. Both are false. Then the passage gives the ruling: Jabriyya are definitely disbelievers because they deny the very basis of religious obligation. For Qadariyya, there is scholarly difference; the preferred opinion is that they are not disbelievers. The reason is that they still affirm that Allah creates the servant's power and will, so ultimately the act is created by Allah. The commentary then notes the grammatical form of 'Jabriyya' and 'Qadariyya'. Finally, it addresses a Qadariyya objection: if Allah creates all actions, then punishing a sinner would be unjust. The Ash'ari response is that punishment is based on the voluntary aspect of the act, which is the 'acquisition' (kasb). The text cuts off at 'which is the acquisition'.

Key Terms
حركة اختيارية
حركة اضطرارية
جبرية
قدرية
كفر
تكليف
جزء اختياري
كسب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Ash'ari position denies any human responsibility, making God responsible for sin.
Correction: Ash'aris affirm 'acquisition' (kasb): the voluntary component of the act is attributed to the human, grounding accountability while maintaining divine creation of all actions.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the Qadariyya?
A) They are definitely disbelievers.
B) They are not disbelievers, though they hold a false belief.
C) They are disbelievers only if they deny predestination.
D) They are considered Muslims without any fault.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari position steers between Jabriyya and Qadariyya by affirming voluntary action and divine creation, with human 'acquisition' as the basis for accountability.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you fail to obey Allah, do you secretly blame His decree to escape the weight of your own choice? How does this lesson's assertion that the difference between voluntary and involuntary is 'self-evident' strip away that excuse? What sin will you stop justifying today?
?
The Qadariyya were so confident in their logic that they called Allah's justice into question. Are there areas in your life where you silently question Allah's justice because you think you deserve better? This lesson forces you to see that punishment is only for the voluntary component—so where is your heart really directing your will?
?
You have just read that the Jabriyya are considered disbelievers because their view nullifies moral accountability. Reflect: when you say 'it was written' to avoid taking responsibility for fixing a flaw in your character, are you not adopting part of their mindset? What concrete action will you take today to assert your voluntary agency in seeking Allah's pleasure, without falling into the opposite extreme?

Refutation of Jabriyya and Qadariyya
Al-Sawi refutes Jabriyya and Qadariyya and gives the ruling on their disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the doctrines of the Jabriyya and Qadariyya, why they are refuted, and the ruling on their disbelief according to Sunni Islam.

Core Idea
Human actions have a voluntary aspect; Jabriyya and Qadariyya both err but differ in rulings.

This passage from al-Sawi's Hashiya refutes two extreme sects on human actions. The Jabriyya deny any human power, while the Qadariyya claim independent effect. The author explains why the first are definitely disbelievers and the second are not, despite their error, due to their affirmation that Allah creates the servant and his capacities.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the author's argument.
Notice the grammatical notes in the latter part.
2
Identify the two errors
Find how the Jabriyya claim absolute compulsion (like a thread in the wind) and how the Qadariyya claim originated power has effect.
3
Understand the rulings
Note that Jabriyya are definitely disbelievers because they negate taklif. For Qadariyya, the correct view is they are not disbelievers.
Why the difference? Because Qadariyya still affirm Allah creates the servant and his capacities.
4
Examine the objection and response
The Qadariyya object that if Allah creates actions, punishing would be unjust. Al-Sawi responds with the concept of kasb (acquisition) as the voluntary part.
This shows how Sunni theology preserves accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والفرق بين الحركة الاختيارية والاضطرارية مما هو بديهي عند عاقل . فبطل قول الجبرية بأنه لا قدرة للعبد تقارن فعلاً له أصلاً، بل هو مجبور ظاهراً وباطناً كالخيط المعلَّق في الهواء، تميله الرِّياح بلا اختيار له في شيء أصلاً، وقول القدرية بتأثير القدرة الحادثة في الأفعال على طبق إرادة العبد. والجبرية كفارٌ قطعاً ؛ لأنَّ مذهبهم ينفي التكليف الذي جاء به الرُّسُل عليهم السَّلام، وفي كفر القدرية خلاف، الأصح عدم كفرهم؛ وإن لزمهم إثبات الشريك الله تعالى، إلا أنَّهم لما أثبتوا الله تعالى خَلْقَ العبد وقدرته وإرادته، صار فعل العبد في الحقيقة مخلوقاً له تعالى. قوله : (فبطل قول الجبريَّة) : بسكون الباء وفتحها وقوله : (وقول القدريَّة) : بالرَّفع معطوف على (قول الجبريَّة). قوله : (بتأثير القدرة الحادثة في الأفعال . . . إلخ) : أي : وبنوا على ذلك أموراً فاسدة باطلة؛ منها : أنَّهم قالوا : لو كانت هذه الأفعال مخلوقة الله كما تقولون لكان تعذيب الله له ظلماً . قلنا : التَّعذيب بالنظر للجزء الاختياري، وهو الكسب.
And the difference between voluntary and involuntary movement is self-evident to any rational person. Thus the statement of the Jabriyya is refuted—that the servant has no power that accompanies his action at all, rather he is compelled outwardly and inwardly like a thread suspended in the air, the winds move it without any choice for it in anything at all—and the statement of the Qadariyya [is refuted]—of the effect of the originated power in actions according to the servant's will. The Jabriyya are definitely disbelievers, because their doctrine negates the obligation (taklīf) brought by the messengers, peace be upon them. Regarding the disbelief of the Qadariyya there is disagreement; the correct view is that they are not disbelievers, even though they are led to affirming a partner to Allah, the Exalted. However, because they affirmed that Allah, the Exalted, creates the servant, his power, and his will, the servant's action becomes in reality created by Him, the Exalted. His saying: ('Thus the statement of the Jabriyya is refuted'): with sukun on the ba' and its fatha. And his saying: ('and the statement of the Qadariyya'): in the nominative, coordinated with 'statement of the Jabriyya'. His saying: ('of the effect of the originated power in actions ... etc.'): meaning: and they built on that corrupt, false matters; among them: they said: if these actions were created by Allah as you say, then Allah's punishment of him would be injustice. We say: punishment is with regard to the voluntary part, and it is acquisition (al-kasb).
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage refutes two heretical sects—Jabriyya (extreme predestinarians) and Qadariyya (free-will advocates)—and gives the ruling on their status in Islam. The author begins by stating that the difference between voluntary and involuntary movement is obvious to any rational person, implying that humans clearly experience a sense of choice. Then he declares that the statement of the Jabriyya is refuted: they claim that a servant has absolutely no power accompanying his action, being completely compelled like a thread in the wind. Similarly, the statement of the Qadariyya is refuted: they claim that the originated power (al-qudra al-ḥāditha) has a real effect in actions according to the servant's will. Next, he issues a ruling: the Jabriyya are definitely disbelievers because their doctrine negates the very concept of religious obligation (taklīf) brought by the prophets. For the Qadariyya, there is scholarly disagreement; the correct view is that they are not disbelievers, even though their position implies a kind of partnership with Allah. Why? Because they affirm that Allah creates the servant, his power, and his will, so the servant's action is ultimately created by Allah. The passage then includes commentary by Al-Sawi explaining the grammar of the main text and an objection: the Qadariyya argue that if actions were created by Allah, then punishing the servant would be unjust. Al-Sawi answers that punishment is only in consideration of the voluntary part (al-juzʾ al-ikhtiyārī), which is the act of 'acquisition' (al-kasb), i.e., the servant's chosen aspect for which he is accountable.

Key Terms

قدرية
كفر
تكليف
كسب
قدرة حادثة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If Allah creates everything, humans have no real choice and punishment is unjust.
Correction: Humans have a voluntary part (kasb) that makes them accountable, and Allah creates both the action and the capacity.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the Qadariyya?
A) They are definitely disbelievers.
B) They are not disbelievers, according to the correct view.
C) They are disbelievers only if they deny predestination.
D) The ruling is unknown.

Key Takeaway
The correct Sunni position is that human actions are created by Allah but acquired by humans, making them responsible without falling into compulsion (Jabri) or independent free will (Qadari).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, do you ever use the excuse of 'Allah willed it' to avoid taking responsibility for your own choices? How does this passage's emphasis on al-juzʾ al-ikhtiyārī challenge you to stop hiding behind predestination?
?
When you sin, do you blame Allah's decree or your own weak will? Which of these two extremes—Jabriyya or Qadariyya—do you lean towards, and what specific step will you take today to align your heart with the truth that you are both dependent on Allah and accountable?
?
This passage says the difference between voluntary and involuntary is self-evident. But have you been living as if you are a helpless thread (like the Jabriyya say) or as if you are independent of Allah (like the Qadariyya say)? Which false belief has taken root in your heart, and what concrete action will you take before you sleep tonight to root it out?
