The Hadith on the Vision of Allah: Tests and Interpretation
Al-Sawi narrates a hadith about the vision of Allah on the Day of Judgment with tests and interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the prophetic hadith that describes the believers' vision of Allah on the Day of Judgment, including the tests they face and the interpretation of the Quranic verse about the uncovering of the shin.

Core Idea
The vision of Allah is real but requires purification from false attachments.

Al-Sawi presents a detailed hadith that illustrates the events of the Day of Judgment regarding the vision of Allah. This passage explains how believers are distinguished from hypocrites through a series of tests involving angelic manifestations. It also links the hadith to the Quranic verse about the uncovering of the shin, showing the interpretive tradition of the early Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith narrative
Read the Arabic passage carefully, following the sequence of events from the calling of nations to the final prostration.
2
Identify the tests
Notice the two angelic manifestations that test the believers, and how they reject them based on the attribute of Allah being 'not confined'.
3
Understand the final vision
Observe that when Allah manifests, believers prostrate while hypocrites cannot, indicating the reality of the vision.
4
Connect to Quranic interpretation
See how the hadith is used to explain the verse 'Yawma yukshafu 'an saq' as the removal of a veil.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ففي السُّنَّة ما يقتضي وقوعها فيها للمؤمنين أيضاً) أي: لما ورد في الحديث ما معناه: ينادي مناد من قبل الله تعالى يوم القيامة : كلُّ أمَّة تتّبع معبودها، فعباد الشَّمس يلقون معها في النَّار، وهكذا كلُّ معبودِ عابده إِلَّا من من الله ،كعيسى، ومريم، وعلي ; فإنَّ من عبدهم يلقى مع شيطانه في النَّار ... إلى أن قال في الحديث: «فتبقى هذه الأمة وفيها منافقوها، فيقولون: لا نبرح حتّى نرى معبودنا، فيتجلى لهم ملك لو وضعت بحار الأرض في نقرة إبهامه لوسعها، فيقول لهم: أنا ربُّكم امتحاناً لهم، فيقولون: نعوذ بالله لست ربَّنا; فإنَّ ربَّنا لا يتحيّز وأنت متحيز ; ثم يتجلى لهم ملك آخر لو وضعت بحار الأرض ومثلها معها في نقرة إبهامه لوسعها، فيقولون له مثل ما قالوا للأول، ثمَّ يتجلَّى الله ، فيخرُّ المؤمنون سجَّداً، فيريد المنافقون السُّجود كالمؤمنين، فلا يقدرون; لأنه يصير ظهوره مطبقاً ، فينادى المنادي : (وَامْتَرُوا الْيَوْمَ أَيُّهَا الْمُجْرِمُونَ )) وهذا معنى قوله تعالى: (يَوْمَ يُكْشَفُ عَن سَاقٍ... الآية (٢) ، فكشف الساق عند الخلف مؤوّل بكشف الحجاب، أو كما قال(۳)
His saying: 'And in the Sunna there is what necessitates its occurrence therein also for the believers': i.e., based on what came in the hadith in meaning: A caller will call from Allah on the Day of Judgment: 'Every nation follows its object of worship.' So the worshippers of the sun will be thrown with it into the Fire, and so on for every object of worship except those who were merciful from Allah, like Jesus, Mary, and Ali; for those who worshipped them will be thrown with their devil into the Fire... until he said in the hadith: 'Then this nation remains, including its hypocrites, and they say: We will not leave until we see our object of worship.' Then an angel appears to them; if the oceans of the earth were placed in the hollow of his thumb, they would fill it, and he says to them: 'I am your lord,' testing them. They say: 'We seek refuge in Allah; you are not our Lord; for our Lord is not confined, and you are confined.' Then another angel appears; if the oceans of the earth and as much again were placed in the hollow of his thumb, they would fill it, and they say the same as they said to the first. Then Allah manifests Himself, and the believers fall down in prostration, and the hypocrites want to prostrate like the believers but cannot, because His manifestation becomes a solid cover. Then a caller calls out: 'Separate yourselves today, O criminals!' (Surah Ya-Sin: 59). And this is the meaning of His saying: 'The day the shin shall be uncovered' (Surah al-Qalam: 42). The uncovering of the shin among the Successors is interpreted as the removal of the veil, or as stated.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the phrase 'and in the Sunna there is what necessitates its occurrence therein also for the believers' from the base text. The author then provides a detailed hadith that describes the events of the Day of Judgment regarding the vision of Allah. It begins with a caller summoning each nation to follow its object of worship. Those who worshipped false deities are cast into the Fire, with exceptions for those who were worshipped without their consent (like Jesus, Mary, Ali). Then the believers (and hypocrites) remain. They demand to see their Lord. They are tested with two different manifestations of angels who claim to be their Lord, but the believers recognize that Allah is not confined and reject them. Finally, Allah manifests Himself, and the believers prostrate, while the hypocrites cannot. This is linked to the Quranic verse 'Yawma yukshafu 'an saq' which is interpreted as the removal of a veil.

Key Terms
تجلى (tajalla)
سجود (sujud)
كشف (kashf)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the hadith describes a physical seeing of Allah in a confined manner.
Correction: The interpretation by the early Muslims (khalaf) is that 'kashf al-saq' means removal of the veil, affirming the vision without physical confinement.

Checkpoint

D) They are tested by a great storm.

Key Takeaway
The hadith affirms the believers' vision of Allah on the Day of Judgment after undergoing tests of faith, and the Quranic verse is interpreted metaphorically as removal of the veil.

?

?

If Allah were to manifest Himself to you now, would you be able to fall in prostration, or would some hidden attachment prevent you? Identify one attachment in your life that you treat almost like an object of worship and commit to breaking it this week.
?
The hadith ends with the separation of the criminals. Do you live as if that separation is inevitable and near, or have you become complacent? Write down one practical change you will make today to be among those who recognize their Lord and prostrate with sincerity.

Zamakhshari's Denial of Ru'ya and His Satirical Poem
Introduces Zamakhshari's denial of ru'ya and quotes his satirical poem against Ahl al-Sunna.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Zamakhshari's Mu'tazilite denial of the vision of Allah and the content of his satirical poem against Ahl al-Sunna.

Core Idea
Zamakhshari's poem shows the Mu'tazilite charge that Ahl al-Sunna are anthropomorphists hiding behind 'balkafa'.

In this passage, the commentator turns to a famous Mu'tazilite scholar, Zamakhshari, who denied the bodily vision of Allah (ru'ya) and composed a scathing poem against Ahl al-Sunna. The poem accuses them of following whims, likening Allah to creation, and cloaking their anthropomorphism with the term 'balkafa.' Understanding this polemic is key to grasping the sectarian debate over divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic text and its literal translation to get the gist of Zamakhshari's accusations.
Pay attention to the poem's tone and terms.
2

Notice the derogatory image of 'tied-up donkeys'.
3
Understand 'balkafa'

This term is central to the Mu'tazilite critique.

The passage is a 'completion' (tamah) to the discussion.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تتمة من جملة ما أنكر رؤية الله تعالى الزَّمخشري في «الكشاف» وأنشد يهجو أهل السُّنَّة بقوله (٣) : لجماعة سـمـوا هـواهـم سـنـة وجـمـاعـة حـمـر لـعـمـري مـوكـفـة قد شبّهوه بخلقه وتخوّفوا شنع الورى فتستّروا بالبلكفة
A completion: Among those who denied the vision of Allah, the Exalted, is al-Zamakhshari in 'al-Kashshaf', and he recited lampooning Ahl al-Sunna with his saying: 'A group who named their whims as Sunna, and a group of tied-up donkeys, by my life, they likened Him to His creation and feared the ugly talk of people, so they veiled themselves with anthropomorphism (balkafa).'
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a completion (tamah) that introduces al-Zamakhshari, the famous Mu'tazilite exegete, as one of those who denied the bodily vision of Allah (ru'ya). In his commentary 'al-Kashshaf', he composed a poem mocking Ahl al-Sunna. The poem accuses Ahl al-Sunna of following their whims and calling it Sunna, likening them to tied-up donkeys. He claims they liken Allah to His creation and, fearing public condemnation, hide behind 'balkafa' (anthropomorphism). The term 'balkafa' is derived from the phrase 'bi-la kayf' (without how), which is a Ash'arite principle for affirming attributes without modality. Zamakhshari uses it derogatorily. The passage sets up the context for the Sunni rejoinders that follow.

Poetic Rebuttals of Zamakhshari by Ibn Munir and Abu Hayyan
Quotes two Sunni poets refuting Zamakhshari's denial of ru'ya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sunni scholars used poetry to rebut the Mu'tazilite denial of seeing Allah (ru'ya), citing the Prophet's permission for poetic defense and key scriptural evidence.

Core Idea
Poetry becomes a tool of theological warfare, defended by prophetic precedent.

This passage presents two poetic rebuttals by Sunni scholars Ibn Munir and Abu Hayyan against Zamakhshari's lampooning of the belief in ru'ya (seeing Allah). Ibn Munir justifies poetic response by citing the Prophet's permission to Hassan ibn Thabit, then mocks the Mu'tazilites for denying Allah's promise. Abu Hayyan directly challenges Zamakhshari's comparison of Sunnis to donkeys, pointing to the verse of al-A'raf as decisive. These verses show that Sunni scholars engaged in the same poetic form to defend orthodoxy.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
The passage is a response to Zamakhshari's poetry denying ru'ya. Notice that both poets are defending the Sunni position against Mu'tazilite denial.
Zamakhshari was a prominent Mu'tazilite scholar who composed lampoons against Sunni beliefs.
2
Analyze Ibn Munir's argument
Ibn Munir first justifies poetic rebuttal by citing the Prophet's permission for Hassan ibn Thabit. Then he states that the Mu'tazilites disbelieve in ru'ya, defying Allah's promise, and calls them not the saved ones.
The phrase 'كفروا برؤية ربهم' is a strong rebuke, but not necessarily declaring apostasy.
3
Analyze Abu Hayyan's rebuttal
Abu Hayyan accuses Zamakhshari of ignorance for likening the early Muslims and people of insight to tied-up donkeys. He insists that the verse of al-A'raf (7:143) is just and supports ru'ya.
The verse of al-A'raf refers to Musa asking to see Allah, implying its possibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ابن المنير حيث انتقل للهجو، فقد أذن النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم لحسان فيه، ونقتدي به فنقول : وجماعة كفروا برؤية ربهم هذا لوعد الله ما لن يخلفه وتلقَّبوا الناجين كلًا إنَّهم إن لم يكونوا في لظى فعلى شفى وقال أبو حيان : شبَّهت جهلاً صدر أمة أحمد وذوي البصائر بالحمير الموكفة وجب الخسار عليك فانظر منصفاً في آية الأعراف فهي المنصفة
Ibn al-Munir said: Since he turned to lampooning, the Prophet ﷺ permitted Hassan [ibn Thabit] to do so, and we follow him and say: 'And a group disbelieved in seeing their Lord; this is by the promise of Allah, which will not fail. And they called themselves the saved ones, but no, if they are not in the blaze, then they are on the brink.' And Abu Hayyan said: 'You ignorantly likened the foremost of the nation of Ahmad and the people of insight to tied-up donkeys. Loss is incumbent upon you; look fairly at the verse of al-A'raf, for it is just.'
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage presents the poetic responses of two Sunni scholars to Zamakhshari's lampoon. First, Ibn al-Munir (Ibn Munir) begins by justifying poetic rebuttal: since Zamakhshari turned to lampoon (al-hija'), and the Prophet ﷺ permitted Hassan ibn Thabit to respond to poetry, they follow that precedent. Then he recites his own poem: 'And a group disbelieved in seeing their Lord' – this refers to the Mu'tazilites who deny ru'ya. He says this is against Allah's promise (the promise of seeing Him in the afterlife) which will not fail. He then mocks them for calling themselves 'the saved ones' (an-Najun, a reference to the Mu'tazilites' claim to be the saved sect), but states they are either in the blaze (Hell) or on the brink. Second, Abu Hayyan responds directly to Zamakhshari's poem: 'You ignorantly likened the foremost of the nation of Ahmad (i.e., the Companions and the righteous) and the people of insight (Ahl al-Sunna) to tied-up donkeys.' He warns that loss is upon Zamakhshari and directs him to look justly at the verse in Surah al-A'raf (7:143) which mentions Musa's request to see Allah, implying that it supports the possibility of ru'ya. The responses show the Sunni stance against the Mu'tazilite denial, using the same poetic form to refute.

Key Terms
رؤية
ابن المنير
أبو حيان
آية الأعراف
الناجين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ibn Munir's use of 'kufr' means the Mu'tazilites are apostates.
Correction: In this context, 'kufr' is a strong rebuke for rejecting a fundamental Sunni belief, not necessarily declaring them outside Islam.

Checkpoint

A) The Prophet's permission to Hassan ibn Thabit
B) Abu Bakr
C) Umar
D) Ali

Key Takeaway
Sunni scholars used poetry, sanctioned by prophetic example, to defend the creed of ru'ya against Mu'tazilite denial.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Obligation to Believe Muhammad is Best and Refutation of Zamakhshari
The author states the obligation to believe Muhammad is best of creation and refutes Zamakhshari's claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Muslims must believe that Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) is the best of all creation, and how scholars refuted al-Zamakhshari's claim that the angel Jibril is superior, using the principle of rhetorical context.

Core Idea
The Qur'an's eloquence refutes al-Zamakhshari by matching speech to its situation.

In this passage, the author establishes a core belief: that Muhammad is the most excellent of all beings. He then addresses a historical controversy sparked by al-Zamakhshari, who argued from Qur'anic verses that Jibril is superior. To refute this, the author invokes the science of balaghah (rhetoric), showing that the verses were not a ranking but a response to accusations. This lesson unpacks that argument and the doctrinal consensus it protects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation to get the overall meaning.
2
Identify the three elements
Find the statement of obligation, the exception (Zamakhshari), and the refutation. Notice how the author moves from consensus to controversy.
3
Understand Zamakhshari's proof
Zamakhshari used Quranic verses where Jibril is described as 'noble messenger' and 'trustworthy', while Muhammad is only called 'not mad'. Why would that imply superiority?
The argument seems textual but ignores context.
4
Grasp the refutation
The author explains that the Quran's eloquence requires matching speech to the situation (mula'amat al-kalam li-muqtaḍa al-hal). The verses were revealed to counter the disbelievers' accusations, not to compare ranks.
Thus, Zamakhshari's literal reading misses the rhetorical purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان مراتب الخلق
ويجب اعتقاد أنّ محمداً صلى الله عليه وسلم وعليهم أجمعين أفضلهم وأنّه آخرهم، ويليه في الفضل : الخصال :قوله : ( أفضلهم أي الأنبياء، ومن باب أولى غيرهم فهو أفضل الخلق على الإطلاق جنّاً وإنساً وملكاً، دنيا وأخرى في جميع بإجماع المسلمين، ما عدا الزَّمخشري ؛ فإنَّه خرق الإجماع، وقال بتفضيل جبريل على محمد و مستدلاً بما في سورة التكوير) من قوله تعالى: إِنَّهُ لَقَولُ رَسُولٍ كَرِيمٍ ... الآية (۱) ، حيث وصف جبريل بأنه رسول كريم إلى قوله : (أمين (۳) ، واقتصر في وصف محمد لله على قوله : (وَمَا صَاحِبُكُم بِمَجْنُونِ ) (۳). فردَّ عليه : بأنَّ القرآن في أعلى طبقات البلاغة ؛ وهي مطابقة الكلام لمقتضى الحال ؛ فإنَّ كلام الكفَّار كان في الواسطة الذي كان يأخذ عنه النَّبيَّ ، حيث قالوا : إنَّما يعلمه بشر، وقالوا : إِنَّ به جِنَّة ؛ أي: أخذاً من الجنّ، فردَّ عليهم المولى بمدح الواسطة وبراءة المصطفى مما يقولون؛ فإنَّه كان معروفاً بينهم بالصَّادق الأمين قال تعالى: أَمْ لَمْ يَعْرِفُوا رَسُوهُمْ فَهُمْ لَهُ منكرون (٤)، وتفضيله دلّ عليه أساطير الأولين والآخرين.
Statement of the ranks of creation. And it is obligatory to believe that Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace and all of them, is the most excellent of them and that he is the last of them, and after him in excellence are the prophets [؟] . He said: (most excellent of them) i.e., of the prophets, and a fortiori of others, for he is the most excellent of creation absolutely, jinn, humans, and angels, in this world and the next in everything [؟] by consensus of Muslims, except for al-Zamakhshari, for he broke the consensus and said that Jibril is superior to Muhammad, adducing from Surah al-Takwir from His statement: 'Indeed, it is the word of a noble messenger' ... the verse (1), where he described Jibril as a noble messenger up to His statement: 'trustworthy' (3), and he confined the description of Muhammad to Allah's statement: 'And your companion is not mad' (3). So he refuted him: that the Quran is at the highest level of eloquence, which is the correspondence of speech to the requirement of the situation; for the speech of the disbelievers was about the intermediary who used to take from the Prophet, where they said: 'Only a human teaches him,' and they said: 'Indeed, he has madness' i.e., taken from the jinn. So the Lord refuted them by praising the intermediary and declaring the Chosen One innocent of what they say; for he was known among them as the truthful, the trustworthy. He said: 'Or did they not recognize their Messenger, so they deny him?' (4). And his superiority is indicated by the legends of the ancients and the later ones.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage begins by stating the obligation to believe that Muhammad (peace be upon him) is the most excellent of all creation, including prophets, humans, jinn, and angels. The author then notes that this is a matter of consensus among Muslims, with the exception of al-Zamakhshari, who broke this consensus by claiming that the angel Jibril (Gabriel) is superior to Muhammad. Zamakhshari's proof is based on verses from Surah al-Takwir, where Allah describes Jibril as a noble messenger (rasul karim) and trustworthy (amin), while describing Muhammad only as 'not mad'. The refutation argues that the Qur'an is at the highest level of eloquence (balaghah), which requires matching speech to context. The disbelievers had accused Muhammad of being taught by a human or being possessed by jinn, so Allah responded by praising Jibril (the intermediary) and clearing Muhammad of their accusations. The context demanded praise of the intermediary and defense of the Prophet, not a comparison of rank. Thus, Zamakhshari's argument is invalid because he ignored the principle of rhetorical appropriateness. The passage concludes that the superiority of Muhammad is established by the traditions of the early and later generations.

Key Terms
أفضلهم
جبريل
رسول كريم
بلاغة
مطابقة الكلام لمقتضى الحال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The refutation of al-Zamakhshari is based on a textual comparison showing that the verses about Jibril are more praiseworthy than those about Muhammad.
Correction: The refutation argues that the verses have different contexts: the verses about Jibril were to refute accusations against the Prophet, not to establish Jibril's superiority. The principle of rhetorical context (mula'amat al-kalam li-muqtaḍa al-hal) shows that the speech is appropriate to the situation, not a ranking.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject al-Zamakhshari's argument that Jibril is superior to Muhammad?
A) Because the verses in Surah al-Takwir are abrogated.
B) Because the context of the verses is to refute the disbelievers' accusations, not to compare rank.
C) Because Jibril is a created being whereas Muhammad is uncreated.
D) Because the consensus of Muslims is that all prophets are equal.

Key Takeaway
The consensus that Muhammad is the best of creation is defended by understanding the Qur'an's eloquence as contextual, not comparative.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran, do you ever find yourself taking verses out of their context, imposing your own assumptions on their meaning? How will you guard against that after learning this lesson?
?
The disbelievers accused the Prophet of being taught by a human or possessed by jinn. What accusations or doubts have you encountered about Allah's revelation or His Messenger, and how does the principle of contextual eloquence help you respond?
?

Ranks of Prophets, Angels, and Companions: Ash'ari vs Maturidi
Enumeration of ranks with sectarian contrast

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different rankings of prophets, angels, and companions according to the Ash'ari and Maturidi schools, and which view is considered preponderant.

Core Idea
Scholars disagree on whether humans or angels are superior; the Maturidi view ranks Prophet Muhammad above all.

This passage from Sanusi's matn outlines the hierarchy of creation. The author first presents the Ash'ari ranking, then offers the Maturidi position as the stronger one. As you read, notice the detailed order and the proof for the Companions' virtue.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic source text and its English translation. Notice the structure: it begins with an overall ranking (Ash'ari) and then gives a more detailed Maturidi ranking.
The footnote markers (٢), (۳), (٤) refer to citations that are not fully included here.
2
Compare the two rankings
Identify the differences. In the Ash'ari ranking, angels come before Companions. In the Maturidi ranking, the Prophet and certain prophets come before angels, and common humans come before common angels.
The author states the Maturidi method is preponderant (rajiha).
3
Understand the Companions' rank
Note that the passage ends with the Companions and their rank relative to angels. According to Ash'ari, Companions follow angels; according to Maturidi, angels are inferior to humans, so Companions are higher.
The passage cites Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus for the Companions' virtue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان مراتب الخلق
أولو العَزْم من الرُّسُل، فبقيّة الرّسل، فالأنبياء، فرؤساء الملائكة، فبقية الملائكة من غير تعيين إذ لا تُعلم الحقيقة، فأصحاب النبي
قوله : (أولو العزم :أي: وهم خمسة ذكرهم الله تعالى في قوله: وَإِذْ أَخَذْنَا مِنَ النَّبِيْنَ مِثَقَهُمْ وَمِنكَ وَمِن نُوحٍ وَإِبْرَاهِيمَ وَمُوسَى وَعِيسَى )
قوله : ( فالأنبياء) : أي : وغير الرُّسل.
قوله : (فبقيَّة الملائكة . . . إلخ ) : هذه طريقة الأشاعرة وهي مرجوحة، وطريقة الماتريدية هي الرَّاجحة، وحاصلها أن تقول : أفضل الخلق نبينا، ثمَّ إبراهيم، ثم موسى، ثمَّ عيسى، ثمَّ نوح، ثمَّ بقيَّة الرُّسل ، ثمَّ الأنبياء غير الرسل، وهم متفاضلون فيما بينهم، لكن لا يعلم تفضيلهم إلَّا الله تعالى، ثم جبريل، ثم إسرافيل، ثمّ ميكائيل، ثمَّ عزرائيل، ثمَّ عامة البشر، ثمَّ عامة الملائكة (٢)
قوله : (فأصحاب النَّبي ) : أي : فمرتبتهم تلي الملائكة على طريقة الأشاعرة، وعلى طريقة الماتريدية الملائكة دون البشر في الفضل، دلَّ على فضلهم الكتاب (۳) ، والسُّنَّة (٤) ، والإجماع، وقرن الصحابة مئة
Statement of the ranks of creation. The possessors of resolve among the messengers, then the rest of the messengers, then the prophets, then the chiefs of the angels, then the rest of the angels without specification, for the reality is not known, then the companions of the Prophet. He said: (The possessors of resolve) i.e., they are five whom Allah mentioned in His statement: 'And when We took from the prophets their covenant and from you and from Noah and Abraham and Moses and Jesus.' He said: (then the prophets) i.e., and those other than messengers. He said: (then the rest of the angels ... etc.): This is the Ash'ari method, and it is weak, and the Maturidi method is the preponderant one, and its summary is that you say: The best of creation is our Prophet, then Abraham, then Moses, then Jesus, then Noah, then the rest of the messengers, then the prophets other than messengers—and they vary in excellence among themselves, but their rank is not known except to Allah—then Jibril, then Israfil, then Mika'il, then 'Azra'il, then the common people, then the common angels (2). He said: (then the companions of the Prophet) i.e., their rank follows the angels according to the Ash'ari method, and according to the Maturidi method, the angels are inferior to humans in virtue. The Book (3), the Sunnah (4), and consensus indicate their virtue, and the generation of the Companions is a hundred [؟].
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the ranks of creation. It begins with an enumeration according to the Ash'ari school: Ulu al-'Azm (messengers with resolve), then other messengers, then prophets, then chief angels, then other angels (without specific ranking), then the Companions. The commentary then explains that Ulu al-'Azm are five: Muhammad, Noah, Abraham, Moses, and Jesus, as indicated by the Qur'anic verse. 'Prophets' here includes those who are not messengers. The author then contrasts this with the Maturidi method, which he declares preponderant (rajiha). The Maturidi ranking is given in detail: Prophet Muhammad, then Abraham, then Moses, then Jesus, then Noah, then the rest of the messengers, then prophets who are not messengers (who are themselves ranked but the order is known only to Allah), then the angels Jibril, Israfil, Mika'il, 'Azra'il, then common humans, then common angels. The passage then discusses the rank of the Companions: according to Ash'aris, they are below the angels; according to Maturidis, angels are below humans in virtue (meaning Companions are superior to angels). The proof for the high rank of the Companions is the Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus. The final phrase 'and the generation of the Companions is a hundred' likely alludes to the hadith 'The best of generations is my generation' (khayr al-qurun qarni).

Key Terms
أولو العزم
الأنبياء
الملائكة
الأشاعرة
الماتريدية
أصحاب النبي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Ash'ari and Maturidi agree on the relative status of angels and humans.
Correction: The passage clarifies that Ash'aris place angels above Companions, while Maturidis place humans (especially the Prophet) above angels.

Checkpoint
According to the preponderant (Maturidi) view, what is the order of excellence among prophets and angels?
A) Muhammad, then Jibril, then Abraham, then other prophets.
B) Muhammad, then Abraham, then Moses, then Jesus, then Noah, then other messengers, then prophets, then Jibril, then other angels.
C) Jibril, then Muhammad, then other messengers, then angels.
D) All prophets and angels are equal in virtue.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi view, which places Prophet Muhammad and the Ulu al-Azm above the angels, is considered preponderant over the Ash'ari ranking.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your heart, do you truly place Prophet Muhammad above all creation, including the angels? If so, how does that affect the way you honor him daily—through salawat, following his sunnah, and defending his honor? If not, what holds you back?
?
The Companions are ranked above common angels in the Maturidi view. Do you feel a greater sense of connection and respect for them because of this? When you read the life of a Sahabi, do you see them as ordinary people or as beings of a higher spiritual station?
?
When two major theological schools differ on a matter like this, it can be unsettling. Which tendency do you notice in yourself: to accept the preponderant view (here Maturidi) and move on, or to remain in doubt? What does your inclination reveal about your trust in scholarly authority and your personal relationship with Allah's revelation?

The Rank of the Companions and Refutation of Deviant Views
Al-Sawi ranks the Companions and refutes the views of al-Khattabiyya and al-Shi'a.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni consensus on the ranking of the Companions and the refutation of deviant views that contradict this ranking.

Core Idea
The Companions are the best of creation after the prophets, with Abu Bakr as the best.

This passage from al-Sawi’s commentary establishes the orthodox Sunni position on the Companions. It first clarifies their rank relative to angels and then affirms the well-known order of the four rightly guided caliphs. The text also explicitly refutes the claims of al-Khattabiyya and al-Shi'a who deviate from this consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the passage once to get a sense of its flow. Notice the two main topics: the rank of Companions and the refutation of sects.
2
Understand the two schools on Companions vs. angels
The passage mentions that according to Ash'aris, Companions rank after angels, but Maturidis consider angels below humans in virtue. This is a subtle theological difference.
The author does not take sides here; he simply reports both views.
3
Identify the evidence for the virtue of Companions
The passage cites the Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus as proofs for their virtue. Also note the duration of the Companionship era (120 years).
4
Learn the ranking and refuted groups
The passage states the best of the Companions is Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali. It refutes al-Khattabiyya (who prefer Umar over Abu Bakr) and al-Shi'a (who prefer Ali over Uthman).
This ranking is a central Sunni belief.
5
Reflect on the theological importance
Understand that this ranking is not arbitrary but based on evidence, and defending it is part of Sunni orthodoxy against sectarian claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأصحاب النبي. قوله : (فأصحاب النَّبي ) : أي : فمرتبتهم تلي الملائكة على طريقة الأشاعرة، وعلى طريقة الماتريدية الملائكة دون البشر في الفضل، دلَّ على فضلهم الكتاب (۳) ، والسُّنَّة (٤) ، والإجماع، وقرن الصحابة مئة وعشرون سنة مبدؤها البعثة . قوله : (وأفضلهم : أبو بكر . . . إلخ) : رد بذلك على الخطابية القائلين بتقديم عمر على أبي بكر، وعلى الشّيعة القائلين بتقديم عليّ على عثمان (۱).
And the Companions of the Prophet. He said: (The Companions of the Prophet): meaning: their rank follows the angels according to the Ash'ari method, and according to the Maturidi method the angels are below humans in virtue, and the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus indicate their virtue, and the era of the Companions is one hundred and twenty years, its beginning is the sending [of the Prophet]. He said: (And the best of them: Abu Bakr... etc.): He refuted by that al-Khattabiyya who say that Umar is superior to Abu Bakr, and al-Shi'a who say that Ali is superior to Uthman.
Source pages p. 352

Commentary
This passage discusses the rank of the Companions of the Prophet. The base text states 'fa ashab al-nabi' (then the Companions of the Prophet). The commentator explains that according to the Ash'ari view, the rank of the Companions comes after the angels, while according to the Maturidi view, angels are below humans in virtue. He then cites evidence from the Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus for the virtue of the Companions, and notes that the era of the Companions lasted one hundred and twenty years starting from the Prophet's mission. Next, he comments on the phrase 'wa afdaluhum Abu Bakr...' (and the best of them is Abu Bakr...). He states that this ranking refutes two deviant groups: al-Khattabiyya, who claim Umar is superior to Abu Bakr, and al-Shi'a, who claim Ali is superior to Uthman. The commentator thus affirms the orthodox Sunni view of the superiority of the first four caliphs in their known order.

Key Terms

أبو بكر
عمر
عثمان
علي
الخطابية
الشيعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that Umar is superior to Abu Bakr (al-Khattabiyya) or that Ali is superior to Uthman (al-Shi'a).
Correction: The passage affirms the Sunni consensus that Abu Bakr is the best, followed by Umar, then Uthman, then Ali.

Checkpoint
Which two groups does Al-Sawi refute in this passage regarding the ranking of the Companions?
A) The Khawarij and the Mu'tazila
B) The Ash'aris and the Maturidis
C) Al-Khattabiyya and al-Shi'a
D) The Jahmiyya and the Qadariyya

Key Takeaway
The first four caliphs in order are the most virtuous of the Companions, and this ranking is a fundamental Sunni belief that refutes sectarian claims.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you find yourself favoring one Companion over another based on family, tribe, or personal achievements rather than the consensus of the Sunnah? How will you realign your heart to accept the ranking taught by the Salaf?
?
The passage refutes those who elevate Umar over Abu Bakr or Ali over Uthman. Have you ever doubted the established order in your heart? What step will you take to uproot any trace of sectarian leaning from your belief?
?
If someone asked you why Abu Bakr is the best of the Companions, could you answer with the evidence from this passage? What keeps you from being prepared to defend this fundamental belief?

The Order of the Four Rightly Guided Caliphs
Sawi states the ranking of the best Companions and refutes two deviant sects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni consensus on the precedence of Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali, and how this refutes deviant sects.

Core Idea
The best of the Companions after the Prophet are Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, then Ali.

This passage establishes the foundational ranking of the Companions according to Ahl al-Sunnah. It directly counters the Khattabiyya who place Umar above Abu Bakr and the Shi'a who place Ali above Uthman.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and literal translation carefully. Notice the concise wording and the immediate refutation of deviant views.
The passage begins with the ranking and then explains its polemical purpose.
2
Identify the order of the four caliphs
List the four names in the order given: Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, Ali. Understand that this order is based on their virtue according to Sunni tradition.
3
Understand the refutations
Note that Sawi refutes two groups: the Khattabiyya (who prefer Umar over Abu Bakr) and the Shi'a (who prefer Ali over Uthman). This shows the passage is not just informative but also defensive.
These refutations are grounded in the consensus of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأفضلهم : أبو بكر ،فعمر فعثمان فعليّ، فبقيّة العشرة، فبقيّةُ البدريين، فأهلُ بيعة الرّضوان، فبقيَّةُ الصَّحابة، وعشرون سنة مبدؤها البعثة . قوله : (وأفضلهم : أبو بكر . . . إلخ) : رد بذلك على الخطابية القائلين . بتقديم عمر على أبي بكر، وعلى الشّيعة القائلين بتقديم عليّ على عثمان (۱). : قوله : (فبقيَّة العشرة :أي: يلون عليّاً في الفضل؛ وهم: طلحة بن عبيد الله ، والزُّبير بن العوام ابن عمة رسول الله ، وعبد الرحمن بن عوف، وسعد بن أبي وقاص، وسعيد بن زيد، وأبو عبيدة عامر ابن الجراح، ولا يعلم تفاوتهم في الفضل إلا الله . قوله : (فبقيَّة البدريين أي فمرتبتهم تلي مرتبة الستة من العشرة، ولا فرق بين من استشهد فيها وهم أربعة عشر رجلاً ؛ ستّة من المهاجرين وثمانية من الأنصار، وجملتهم ثلاث مئة وثلاثة عشر وقيل: وخمسة عشر، وقيل : وسبعة عشر، وقيل: وتسعة عشر، وإنما قال : وبقيَّة البدريين؛ لأنَّ العشرة رؤساء أهل بدر. قوله: (فأهل بيعة الرضوان أسقط الشَّرح أهل أحد الذين لم يحضروا بدراً، وهم أفضل من أهل بيعة الرّضوان الذين لم يحضروا بدراً ولا أحداً، وكانوا ألفاً وأربع مئة ، وقيل : وخمس مئة . (( (1) ينظر شرح صحيح مسلم للنووي (١٤٨/١٥). ))
And the best of them: Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali, then the rest of the ten, then the rest of the Badriyyin, then the people of the Pledge of Ridwan, then the rest of the Companions, and twenty years, its beginning is the mission. His saying: (And the best of them: Abu Bakr ... etc.): He refuted by that the Khattabiyya who say that Umar is superior to Abu Bakr, and the Shi'a who say that Ali is superior to Uthman (1). His saying: (the rest of the ten): i.e., they follow Ali in virtue; they are: Talha ibn Ubaydillah, al-Zubayr ibn al-Awwam the cousin of the Messenger of Allah, Abdurrahman ibn Awf, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, Sa'id ibn Zayd, and Abu Ubayda Amir ibn al-Jarrah, and their differentiation in virtue is not known except to Allah. His saying: (the rest of the Badriyyin): i.e., their rank follows the rank of the six from the ten, and there is no distinction between those who were martyred therein, who are fourteen men: six from the Muhajirun and eight from the Ansar, and their total is three hundred and thirteen; and it is said: fifteen, and it is said: seventeen, and it is said: nineteen. And he only said: the rest of the Badriyyin, because the ten are the leaders of the people of Badr. His saying: (the people of the Pledge of Ridwan) – the commentary omitted the people of Uhud who did not attend Badr, and they are better than the people of the Pledge of Ridwan who did not attend Badr or Uhud, and they were one thousand and four hundred, and it is said: five hundred. (( (1) See Sharh Sahih Muslim by al-Nawawi (15/148). ))
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage details the ranking of the best Companions according to Ahl al-Sunnah. It begins by listing the order: Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali, then the rest of the ten (the other six of the ten promised Paradise), then the rest of the participants of Badr (excluding the ten), then the people of the Pledge of Ridwan, then the rest of the Companions. It also mentions that the period of the Companions' virtue spans twenty years from the beginning of the mission. The commentary then explains each category: the refutation of the Khattabiyya (who prefer Umar over Abu Bakr) and the Shi'a (who prefer Ali over Uthman); the names of the remaining six of the ten promised Paradise; the details of the Badriyyin (the participants of Badr) – their number (313 with variations), and that the six from the ten are considered their leaders; and finally the people of the Pledge of Ridwan, noting that the people of Uhud (who missed Badr but were present at Uhud) are ranked above them. The passage also includes a footnote reference to al-Nawawi's commentary on Sahih Muslim.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe Umar is the best Companion after the Prophet, or that Ali is better than Uthman.
Correction: Sunni consensus holds Abu Bakr as best, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali.

Checkpoint
According to Sawi, who is the best of the Companions after the Prophet?
A) Umar
B) Abu Bakr
C) Ali
D) Uthman

Key Takeaway
The Sunni ranking of the best Companions begins with Abu Bakr, followed by Umar, Uthman, and Ali, and this order refutes deviant sects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about the best of the Companions, do you find yourself secretly favoring one over another based on your own inclination rather than the established consensus? Ask yourself: have I truly submitted my heart to what Allah and His scholars have agreed upon? Commit today to silence your personal preference and accept the truth.
?
The passage refutes those who placed Umar above Abu Bakr or Ali above Uthman. Have you ever, even unintentionally, held a view that undermines the rank of any Companion? If so, repent and align your belief with the Sunni creed. Write down one specific step you will take to learn more about the virtues of the Companions as taught by Ahl al-Sunnah.
?
Knowing that deviant sects existed only to be refuted, examine your own heart: are you grateful for being guided to the correct belief about the Companions? Or do you take it for granted? Spend five minutes thanking Allah for protecting you from such misguidance and pray for steadfastness.

The Remaining Ten Promised Paradise
Sawi identifies the six Companions who complete the ten promised Paradise and notes their relative virtue is unknown.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will know who the remaining six of the ten promised Paradise are and that their exact ranking is known only to Allah.

Core Idea
After the four caliphs, the next best are the other six of the ten promised Paradise.

After naming the top four, Sawi lists the remaining six Companions who were promised Paradise. He emphasizes that their precise order of virtue is not definitively known.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Note that the phrase 'the rest of the ten' refers to those who follow Ali in virtue.
2
Memorize the six names
List the six Companions: Talha, Zubayr, Abdurrahman, Sa'd, Sa'id, Abu Ubayda. Understand that they are from the ten promised Paradise.
The other four of the ten are Abu Bakr, Umar, Uthman, and Ali.
3
Understand the humility of knowledge
Notice the statement that their exact ranking is known only to Allah. This teaches that while we know they are together in virtue, we do not claim to know who is best among them.
This guards against unnecessary disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(( (1) ينظر شرح صحيح مسلم للنووي (١٤٨/١٥). ))
And the best of them: Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali, then the rest of the ten, then the rest of the Badriyyin, then the people of the Pledge of Ridwan, then the rest of the Companions, and twenty years, its beginning is the mission. His saying: (And the best of them: Abu Bakr ... etc.): He refuted by that the Khattabiyya who say that Umar is superior to Abu Bakr, and the Shi'a who say that Ali is superior to Uthman (1). Commentary

It begins by listing the order: Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali, then the rest of the ten (the other six of the ten promised Paradise), then the rest of the participants of Badr (excluding the ten), then the people of the Pledge of Ridwan, then the rest of the Companions. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the exact ranking of the six Companions not specified?
A) Because they are all equal
B) Because only Allah knows their differentiation in virtue
C) Because the Prophet did not mention it
D) Because they are less virtuous than the Badriyyin

Key Takeaway
After the four caliphs, the next best are the remaining six of the ten promised Paradise, whose precise ranking is known only to Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about the Companions, do you ever find yourself speculating about who is better than whom? How does the statement 'only Allah knows their differentiation' challenge your attitude?
?
The Prophet ﷺ promised Paradise to these ten. Yet we are not told the exact order. What does this teach you about trusting Allah's knowledge over your own curiosity?
?
Do you treat the Companions as a group with shared virtue, or do you secretly elevate some over others based on your own preferences? How can you align your heart with the Sunni approach of withholding judgement where Allah has not spoken?

The Participants of Badr (Badriyyin)
Sawi explains the rank and number of the participants of Badr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the high rank of the participants of the Battle of Badr and their placement in the hierarchy after the ten promised Paradise.

Core Idea
The participants of Badr are the next best after the ten, and their number is 313 with some variations.

Sawi now turns to the Badriyyin, the Companions who fought at the Battle of Badr. He explains their rank, numbers, and notes that the ten are considered their leaders.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic carefully. Note that Sawi says 'the rest of the Badriyyin' because the ten are already included among them and are their leaders.
2
Understand the ranking
The Badriyyin rank after the six of the ten (i.e., after the ten as a group). They include both those who were martyred at Badr and those who survived.
3
Learn the number and details
The total is 313, with some reports adding a few. Also, 14 were martyred: 6 Muhajirun and 8 Ansar.
These numbers are important in Islamic history.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأفضلهم : أبو بكر ،فعمر فعثمان فعليّ، فبقيّة العشرة، فبقيّةُ البدريين، فأهلُ بيعة الرّضوان، فبقيَّةُ الصَّحابة، وعشرون سنة مبدؤها البعثة . قوله : (وأفضلهم : أبو بكر . . . إلخ) : رد بذلك على الخطابية القائلين . بتقديم عمر على أبي بكر، وعلى الشّيعة القائلين بتقديم عليّ على عثمان (۱). : قوله : (فبقيَّة العشرة :أي: يلون عليّاً في الفضل؛ وهم: طلحة بن عبيد الله ، والزُّبير بن العوام ابن عمة رسول الله ، وعبد الرحمن بن عوف، وسعد بن أبي وقاص، وسعيد بن زيد، وأبو عبيدة عامر ابن الجراح، ولا يعلم تفاوتهم في الفضل إلا الله . قوله : (فبقيَّة البدريين أي فمرتبتهم تلي مرتبة الستة من العشرة، ولا فرق بين من استشهد فيها وهم أربعة عشر رجلاً ؛ ستّة من المهاجرين وثمانية من الأنصار، وجملتهم ثلاث مئة وثلاثة عشر وقيل: وخمسة عشر، وقيل : وسبعة عشر، وقيل: وتسعة عشر، وإنما قال : وبقيَّة البدريين؛ لأنَّ العشرة رؤساء أهل بدر. قوله: (فأهل بيعة الرضوان أسقط الشَّرح أهل أحد الذين لم يحضروا بدراً، وهم أفضل من أهل بيعة الرّضوان الذين لم يحضروا بدراً ولا أحداً، وكانوا ألفاً وأربع مئة ، وقيل : وخمس مئة . (( (1) ينظر شرح صحيح مسلم للنووي (١٤٨/١٥). ))
And the best of them: Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali, then the rest of the ten, then the rest of the Badriyyin, then the people of the Pledge of Ridwan, then the rest of the Companions, and twenty years, its beginning is the mission. His saying: (And the best of them: Abu Bakr ... etc.): He refuted by that the Khattabiyya who say that Umar is superior to Abu Bakr, and the Shi'a who say that Ali is superior to Uthman (1). His saying: (the rest of the ten): i.e., they follow Ali in virtue; they are: Talha ibn Ubaydillah, al-Zubayr ibn al-Awwam the cousin of the Messenger of Allah, Abdurrahman ibn Awf, Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, Sa'id ibn Zayd, and Abu Ubayda Amir ibn al-Jarrah, and their differentiation in virtue is not known except to Allah. His saying: (the rest of the Badriyyin): i.e., their rank follows the rank of the six from the ten, and there is no distinction between those who were martyred therein, who are fourteen men: six from the Muhajirun and eight from the Ansar, and their total is three hundred and thirteen; and it is said: fifteen, and it is said: seventeen, and it is said: nineteen. And he only said: the rest of the Badriyyin, because the ten are the leaders of the people of Badr. His saying: (the people of the Pledge of Ridwan) – the commentary omitted the people of Uhud who did not attend Badr, and they are better than the people of the Pledge of Ridwan who did not attend Badr or Uhud, and they were one thousand and four hundred, and it is said: five hundred. (( (1) See Sharh Sahih Muslim by al-Nawawi (15/148). ))
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage details the ranking of the best Companions according to Ahl al-Sunnah. It begins by listing the order: Abu Bakr, then Umar, then Uthman, then Ali, then the rest of the ten (the other six of the ten promised Paradise), then the rest of the participants of Badr (excluding the ten), then the people of the Pledge of Ridwan, then the rest of the Companions. It also mentions that the period of the Companions' virtue spans twenty years from the beginning of the mission. The commentary then explains each category: the refutation of the Khattabiyya (who prefer Umar over Abu Bakr) and the Shi'a (who prefer Ali over Uthman); the names of the remaining six of the ten promised Paradise; the details of the Badriyyin (the participants of Badr) – their number (313 with variations), and that the six from the ten are considered their leaders; and finally the people of the Pledge of Ridwan, noting that the people of Uhud (who missed Badr but were present at Uhud) are ranked above them. The passage also includes a footnote reference to al-Nawawi's commentary on Sahih Muslim.

Key Terms
البدريون
بدر
المهاجرون
الأنصار
ثلاث مئة وثلاثة عشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Badriyyin include only the martyrs, but Sawi clarifies all participants are included.
Correction: All 313 participants of Badr are honored, martyred or not.

Checkpoint

A) 10
B) 14
C) 313
D) 6

Key Takeaway
The participants of Badr rank after the ten promised Paradise, totaling 313 with 14 martyrs, and the ten are their leaders.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Sawi carefully lists the martyrs of Badr—six from the Muhajirun and eight from the Ansar—and says there is no distinction in rank between the living and the martyred. Are you as eager to be among those who serve Allah even if it costs your life? What keeps you back, and what would it take to remove that barrier?
?
The ten promised Paradise are called the 'leaders of the people of Badr.' Do you look to these Companions as your leaders? When you face a difficult choice, does their example weigh on your heart, or do you follow the opinions of people who care nothing for Allah's Messenger?
?
The number of Badriyyin is given with variations—313, 315, 317, 319—yet Sawi does not reject any report. When you hear differing accounts of Islamic history, do you rush to dismiss some as false, or do you hold them all with respect, trusting that Allah preserved what matters? Is your heart at peace with what Allah has chosen to convey?

The People of the Pledge of Ridwan and Others
Sawi places the people of the Pledge of Ridwan in the hierarchy and compares them with those of Uhud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ranking of the people of the Pledge of Ridwan and how the people of Uhud rank above them.

Core Idea
The people of the Pledge of Ridwan are next after the Badriyyin, but those present at Uhud are ranked higher.

Sawi continues the hierarchy by mentioning the people of the Pledge of Ridwan. He notes a comparative point: those who participated in the Battle of Uhud (but not Badr) are better than those who only participated in the Pledge of Ridwan.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic. Notice that the commentary (sharh) omitted the people of Uhud, but Sawi explains their rank relative to the people of Ridwan.
2
Understand the ranking
After the Badriyyin come the people of the Pledge of Ridwan. However, those who were at Uhud (but not Badr) are better than those who only attended the Pledge of Ridwan (and missed Badr and Uhud).
3
Learn the number
The people of Ridwan numbered 1400 or 1500.
This is a large number of Companions.

The Maliki Position on the Formula of the Shahadah
Al-Sawi reports the Maliki school's view on the sufficiency of any wording indicating tawhid and risala for worldly judgments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Maliki school's view on the formula of the shahadah for worldly rulings and the rationale behind it.

Core Idea
For worldly judgments, any wording indicating tawhid and risala suffices.

This passage from al-Sawi clarifies a practical legal question: what form of words is required when someone declares the shahadah for the purpose of worldly rulings? The Maliki school holds a lenient view, as opposed to some others. Let's examine the evidence and reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own flow come through before you interpret.
Notice the footnote markers (١), (٢), (٣) indicating scholastic transmission.
2
Identify the Maliki position and the opposing view
Find the sentence that states the Maliki criterion. Then note who opposed it (Ibn Arafa) and who supported a similar view (al-Ramli, al-Nawawi).
The passage contrasts the Maliki view with those who stipulate a specific wording.
3
Understand the rationale
The last sentence provides the reason: inner attestation is hidden, so an outward sign is needed for worldly rulings. Reflect on why this supports any wording indicating tawhid and risala.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال شيخنا الأمير : سمعنا من المشايخ كثيراً : أنَّ المدار عند المالكية على أي لفظ يفيد الوحدانية والرِّسالة، ونقله اللقاني في «شرحه» عن الأبي (١) مخالفاً لشيخه ابن عرفة (٢) المشترط اللفظ المخصوص، ونحوه للرّملي وجماعة من الشَّافعيَّة، ونحو ما للأبي للنووي) (٣). 
 لإجراء الأحكام الدُّنيويَّة ; لأنَّ التَّصديق لخفائه – بكونه قلبياً – لا بدَّ له من علامة ظاهرة تدلُّ عليه.
Our master al-Amir said: We heard from the mashayikh frequently that the criterion among the Malikis is any wording that indicates oneness and prophethood, and al-Laqqani transmitted in his 'Sharh' from al-Abi (1), opposing his shaykh Ibn Arafa (2) who stipulated the specific wording, and similar is from al-Ramli and a group of the Shafi'is, and similar to what is for al-Abi is for al-Nawawi) (3). For the execution of worldly judgments; because attestation, due to its hiddenness – being internal – necessarily has an outward sign indicating it.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage reports the position of the Maliki school regarding the formula for uttering the two shahadahs. Al-Sawi quotes his teacher al-Amir stating that the Malikis consider any expression that conveys the meaning of the oneness of Allah and the prophethood of Muhammad as sufficient. He then notes that al-Laqqani transmitted this view from al-Abi, who opposed his own teacher Ibn Arafa, who insisted on a specific formula. Al-Ramli and a group of Shafi'is held a similar view to al-Abi, and al-Nawawi likewise. The passage then provides the rationale: an outward sign is needed for the application of worldly legal rulings because inner attestation is imperceptible. Thus, the requirement of utterance for worldly purposes is justified regardless of the exact form.

Key Terms
المالكية
الوحدانية
الرِّسالة
اللفظ المخصوص
الأبي
ابن عرفة
الرملي
النووي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think any utterance is acceptable for the validity of iman itself.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the leniency applies only to worldly legal rulings ('li ijra' al-ahkam al-duniyawiyya'), not to the inner reality of faith.

Checkpoint
According to the Maliki school as reported, what suffices for the utterance of the shahadah in worldly judgments?
A) The exact Arabic phrase as long as it is understood
B) Any wording that indicates tawhid and risala
C) A specific formula taught by the Prophet
D) Only the testimony in Arabic

Key Takeaway
The Maliki school allows any wording indicating tawhid and risala for the shahadah in worldly judgments, because inner faith requires an outward sign.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you encountered someone who expressed belief in a way unfamiliar to you, would you accept their statement as sufficient for worldly dealings? What does your answer reveal about your attachment to form over substance?
?
The Maliki position shows generosity in accepting any wording. Are you as generous in judging others' faith, or do you demand specific phrases and forms? How does your posture mirror or oppose the lesson's principle?

Sins: Major and Minor, Indicators and Elevating Factors
Al-Sawi divides sins into major and minor, refuting Murji'a and Khawarij, and gives indicators of major sins and factors that upgrade minor sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni classification of sins into major and minor, the refutation of extreme views, and the indicators that identify major sins and what can turn a minor sin into a major one.

Core Idea
Sins are not all equal; only the balanced Sunni view preserves both mercy and justice.

Al-Sawi begins by clarifying a point in the base text about even small sins requiring repentance, which leads to the fundamental division of sins into major and minor. This classification is the standard Sunni position, and he immediately defends it against two extreme sects: the Murji'a, who trivialize all sins, and the Khawarij, who exaggerate every sin into disbelief. After establishing the division, he provides practical indicators for recognizing major sins and warns that minor sins can become major through certain attitudes.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it, then read the English translation. Let the author's own progression come through before you interpret.
Notice the opening phrase 'even if small' connects to the preceding lesson on repentance.
2
Identify the two deviant sects and their refutation
Find where Al-Sawi mentions the Murji'a and the Khawarij. Note their opposing views and how the Sunni position is the balanced middle path.
The Murji'a say no sin harms with faith; the Khawarij say every sin is major and makes one a disbeliever.
3
List the indicators of major sins
Al-Sawi gives four signs (amarat) that a sin is major: fixed legal penalty, threat of Fire, description as fasiq, and being cursed in the text. Write them down.
These indicators come after 'وإنَّما لها أمارات'.
4
Understand what elevates a minor sin
Go to the end of the passage where Al-Sawi lists factors that can turn a minor sin into a major one: persistence, taking it lightly, rejoicing, boasting.
This shows that minor sins are not inherently fixed; their context matters.
5
Reflect on the balanced Sunni position
Consider how this classification avoids the extremes of the Murji'a and Khawarij, and how the indicators provide objective criteria for judging severity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ولو صغيرة :أي: هذا إذا كان كبيرة بل ولو صغيرة، وفي کلامه إشارة إلى أنَّ الذُّنوب قسمان: صغائر وكبائر، وهو مذهب أهل السنة، ففيه ردُّ على المرجئة القائلين : إنَّ الذُّنوب كلَّها صغائر، ولا يضرُّ مع الإيمان ذنب، وعلى الخوارج حيث قالوا : إنَّ كلَّ ذنب كبيرة ومرتكبها كافر . واعلم أنَّ الكبائر لا تحصر ،بعدد وإنَّما لها أمارات؛ منها : إيجاب : الحدّ، ومنها : الإيعاد عليها بالعذاب بالنَّار ونحوها، ومنها : وصف فاعلها بالفسق نصاً، ومنها : اللعن كلعن السارق، وأكبرها الكفر بالله تعالى، ثمَّ القتل العمد، وما خرج عن حد الكبيرة وضابطها فهو صغيرة، ولا تحصر أفرادها، وربَّما تقلب الصَّغيرة كبيرة بأمور منها: الإصرار، والتهاون، والفرح، والافتخار بها.
His saying (even if small): i.e., this if it is a major sin, nay even if small; and in his speech there is an indication that sins are two kinds: minor and major, and this is the school of the Ahl al-Sunna; in it is a refutation of the Murji'a who say that all sins are minor, and no sin harms with faith; and against the Khawarij who say that every sin is major and its perpetrator is a disbeliever. And know that major sins are not limited by number but rather have indicators: among them the imposition of the legal fixed penalty; among them the threat with punishment of the Fire and the like; among them describing the doer as a transgressor (fasiq) in the text; among them cursing, such as cursing the thief; and the greatest of them is disbelief in Allah the Exalted; then intentional murder; and whatever falls outside the definition of a major sin and its standard is a minor sin; and its individual instances are not limited; and perhaps a minor sin is turned into a major one by matters: among them persistence, taking it lightly, rejoicing in it, and boasting about it.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage explains the division of sins into major (kaba'ir) and minor (sagha'ir), responding to two deviant sects. The author starts by glossing the base text's expression 'even if small', showing that repentance is required for both categories; this implies the established Sunni position that sins are of two types. The Murji'a falsely held that all sins are minor and do not harm the believer's faith; the Khawarij went to the opposite extreme, claiming every sin is major and renders its doer a disbeliever. Both are refuted. Next, the author provides indicators (amarat) by which major sins are recognized, since they are not confined to a fixed number: (1) the prescription of a fixed legal penalty (hadd), (2) the threat of punishment in the Fire, (3) explicit textual description of the doer as fasiq, and (4) curse (la‘n) such as the curse on a thief. The greatest major sin is disbelief (kufr), followed by intentional murder. Everything that does not meet these criteria is a minor sin, and its individual instances are countless. Importantly, a minor sin can become major due to factors like persistence (israr), taking it lightly (tahawun), rejoicing in it (farah), or boasting about it (iftikhar).

Key Terms
صغائر
كبائر
المرجئة
الخوارج
الحدّ
الفسق
اللعن
الإصرار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Minor sins can never become major; they remain minor regardless of context.
Correction: Al-Sawi explicitly states that minor sins can become major due to persistence, taking them lightly, rejoicing, or boasting. Context and attitude matter.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT mentioned as an indicator of a major sin?
A) Imposition of a fixed legal penalty (hadd)
B) Threat of punishment in the Fire
C) Cursing the doer, as in cursing a thief
D) Boasting about committing the sin

Key Takeaway
The Sunni position on sins is balanced: sins are not all equal, major sins are identified by clear indicators, and minor sins can become major through persistence or pride.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What minor sin have you been persisting in, thinking it is harmless? Will you resolve tonight to stop, before it becomes a major sin in Allah's sight?
?
Do you ever feel a secret pride or joy when you recount a sin? That very emotion, as this lesson warns, can turn it into a major transgression. What will you do to guard your heart against such pleasure?
?
Which of the four upgrading factors—persistence, taking lightly, rejoicing, or boasting—is most present in your life right now? Name one concrete change you will make this week to overturn it.

The Path of the Righteous Predecessors: Creed, Knowledge, and Action
Defines the path of the righteous predecessors in three components and mentions a sign of true guidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the essential components of the path of the righteous predecessors as consisting of correct creed, religious knowledge, and action in accordance with that knowledge, and recognize the sign of true guidance through the blessing and righteousness visible on a guide's companions.

Core Idea
Righteous guidance merges creed, knowledge, and action into one path.

This lesson introduces the foundational way of the righteous predecessors (salaf salih), which every seeker of truth is encouraged to follow. The author defines this path clearly: it is not mere asceticism or scholarship alone, but a combination of correct belief (i'tiqad), sound knowledge (ilm), and consistent practice (amal). Additionally, the text highlights a practical indicator of following this path: the appearance of blessing and righteousness on one’s companions. This is a powerful reminder that the company we keep reflects the path we tread.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text and its translation to grasp the definition of the path.
Notice how the author connects the sign of blessing to the command to follow the path.
2
Identify the three components
Look for the three elements: creed, knowledge, and action. Note that the author emphasizes they are limited to these.
3
Understand the sign of blessing
Notice the statement about blessing appearing on the guide's followers. Think about why this is mentioned as a consequence of following the path.
This sign indicates that the guide is truly on the path of the righteous predecessors.

The Four Established Schools of the Later Imams
Describes the split of later imams into three groups and the emergence of the four established madhhabs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that after the righteous predecessors, the imams who must be followed split into three groups, and among them only the schools of the four imams (Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanafi, Hanbali) became established as the approved madhhabs.

Core Idea
Only four schools of jurisprudence became the approved orthodox madhhabs.

After describing the way of the righteous predecessors, the author turns to the generations that followed. He states that the imams of the nation, who are obligatory to follow, divided into three groups. However, he only details one group: those who dedicated themselves to explaining the practical legal rulings. Among this group, only the schools of four imams—Malik, al-Shafi'i, Abu Hanifa, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal—became firmly established as the accepted schools. This lesson examines this classification and its implications for Islamic legal tradition.

The other two groups are not explained, perhaps because they are less known or not relevant to the discussion.
3
List the four imams
Find the names of the imams whose schools became established. Understand that these four are the founders of the widely accepted madhhabs.
The passage explicitly names Imam Malik, al-Shafi'i, Abu Hanifa, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal.

The Three Groups of Later Imams: Fiqh, Aqeedah, and Tasawwuf
Al-Sawi enumerates three groups of later imams with their roles and exemplars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three specialized groups of imams after the Salaf: those dedicated to fiqh, those dedicated to aqeedah, and those dedicated to tasawwuf, and see how they are complementary.

Core Idea
Later imams specialized into three complementary schools: fiqh, aqeedah, and tasawwuf.

After describing the comprehensive way of the Salaf—combining belief, knowledge, and action—al-Sawi explains that later imams, who must be followed, subdivided into three specialized groups. Each group focuses on one aspect of the religion while remaining within the Salaf's framework. Let's read the passage to see these groups and their exemplars.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once to get a feel for al-Sawi's classification. Focus on the three groups listed.
The third group's name is cut off in the manuscript; note the incomplete name.
2
Identify the three groups
Look for the phrases 'فرقة نصبت نفسها' which introduce each group. Note their respective specialties and key figures.
The first group: fiqh (four imams); second: aqeedah (Ash'ari and Maturidi); third: tasawwuf (imam unnamed).
3
Understand their complementarity
Consider how the three groups together cover the three dimensions of religion: belief, knowledge, and action. The third group's focus on spiritual works completes the first two.
This shows that these groups are not contradictory but interdependent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأن تظهر على أصحابه البركة والصَّلاح، وهذا مأخوذ من قولنا : ( واتبع) في سيرك ( سبيل) أي: طريق (النّاسكين) ناسك ؛ أي عابد (العُلما) جمع عالم، وهو العارف بالأحكام الشَّرعيَّة التي عليها مدار صحة الدِّين، اعتقاديَّة كانت أو عمليَّة، والمراد بهم و السَّلف الصَّالح ومن تبعهم بإحسان وسبيلهم منحصر في اعتقاد وعلم وعمل على طبق العلم . وافترق من جاء بعدهم من أئمة الأمَّة الذين يجب اتِّباعهم على ثلاث فرق : - فرقة نصبت نفسها لبيان الأحكام الشَّرعيّة العمليّة، وهم الأئمة الأربعة وغيرهم من المجتهدين، لكن لم يستقرَّ من المذاهب المرضيَّة سوی مذاهب الأئمة الأربعة . قوله : (وأن تظهر على أصحابه البركة والصَّلاح) أي: لما قيل من الطويل] عن المرء لا تسل وسل عن قرينه فكل قـريـن بـالـمـقـارن يقتدي - وفرقة نصبت نفسها للاشتغال ببيان العقائد التي كان عليها السَّلف، وهم الأشعري والماتريدي ومن تبعهما . - وفرقة نصبت نفسها للاشتغال بالعمل والمجاهدات على طبق ما ذهب إليه الفرقتان المتقدمتان، وهم الإمام [؟]
And that blessing and righteousness appear upon his companions, and this is taken from our statement: And follow in your conduct the path of the devout, i.e., the way of the worshiper, i.e., the worshiper; and 'al-ʿulamā' (the scholars) is the plural of ʿālim, who is the knower of the legal rulings on which the soundness of religion turns, whether creedal or practical. And what is meant by them is the righteous predecessors (salaf) and those who followed them in excellence, and their way is summed up in belief, knowledge, and action in accordance with knowledge. And those who came after them among the imams of the nation, whom it is obligatory to follow, split into three groups: - A group that set itself to explain the practical legal rulings, and they are the four imams and other mujtahids, but from the approved schools only the schools of the four imams became established. His statement: 'And that blessing and righteousness appear upon his companions', meaning it was said: [from the ṭawīl meter] 'Do not ask about the man, ask about his companion; for every companion is guided by his companion.' - A group that set itself to expound the beliefs that the predecessors were upon, and they are al-Ashʿarī, al-Māturīdī, and those who follow them. - A group that set itself to engage in spiritual works and struggles in accordance with what the two preceding groups held, and they are the Imam [?]
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage is a classification and definition. The author begins by explaining the goal of the supplication that blessing and righteousness appear on the Prophet's companions, linking it to the principle of following the righteous. He then defines 'scholars' as those who know the legal rulings that preserve religion, both creedal and practical. He clarifies that the term here refers to the righteous predecessors (Salaf) and their followers, whose comprehensive way is belief, knowledge, and action. Next, he states that the later imams—those who must be followed—split into three specialized groups. The first group focuses on practical legal rulings (fiqh), namely the four imams (Abū Ḥanīfa, Mālik, al-Shāfiʿī, Aḥmad ibn Ḥanbal) and other mujtahids, though only the four schools became established. The author then interjects a commentary on the original phrase about blessing and companions, citing a poetic line: 'Do not ask about the man, ask about his companion...' The second group specializes in creed (ʿaqīda) as held by the Salaf, represented by al-Ashʿarī and al-Māturīdī. The third group specializes in spiritual struggle (mujāhadāt) and works (ʿamal) consistent with the first two groups; their exemplar is mentioned but cut off in the text.

Key Terms
السَّلف الصَّالح
الأئمة الأربعة
الأشعري
الماتريدي
المجاهدات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The three groups are contradictory or one is more important than the others.
Correction: They are complementary specializations covering different aspects of the same Salafī path: belief, knowledge, and action.

Checkpoint

D) One group: the Salaf only

Key Takeaway
The later imams divided into three complementary schools: fiqh, aqeedah, and tasawwuf, each preserving a dimension of the Salaf's way.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Three Groups and the Saved Sect
The saved sect is identified as those combining Sunni creed, legal school adherence, and Junaydi spirituality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the threefold criterion for salvation in traditional Sunni Islam: correct creed according to Ahl al-Sunna, adherence to one of the four legal schools, and following the spiritual path of al-Junayd.

Core Idea
Salvation requires sound creed, correct practice, and spiritual purification.

This passage concludes the discussion of sects by identifying who is saved. It emphasizes that salvation is not merely a matter of belonging to a group, but requires a combination of correct belief, practical adherence to a recognized school, and following the spiritual path of the early Sufis. The author presents a holistic vision of Islamic orthodoxy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage slowly, noting the three elements listed. Pay attention to the order in which they appear.
The passage uses 'thumma' (then) to sequence the elements.
2
Identify the three components
List the three criteria: creed (Ahl al-Sunna), practice (one of four imams), and spiritual path (Junayd). Notice that each is introduced with a specific phrase.
3
Consider the order and relationship
Reflect on why creed comes first, then practice, then spiritual path. What does the phrase 'completion of blessing' imply about the relationship?
The spiritual path is presented as the perfection of the first two.
4
Connect to broader kalam
Think about how this passage ties together 'ilm al-kalam (creed), fiqh (jurisprudence), and tasawwuf (spirituality). It provides a unified vision of salvation.
This reflects the traditional Sunni synthesis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهؤلاء الفِرَق الثَّلاثة هم خواص الأمة المحمديَّة، ومن عداهم من الفرق على ضلال وإن كان البعض منهم يُحكم له بالإسلام، فالنَّاجي من كان في عقيدته على طبق ما بيَّنه أهل السُّنَّة، وقلَّد في الأحكام العمليَّة إماماً من الأئمة الأربعة المرضيَّة، ثمَّ تمامُ النِّعمة والنَّجاة في سلوك مسلك الجنيد وأتباعه بعد أن أحكم دينه على طبق ما بيَّنه الفريقان المتقدِّمان، وممن سلك مسلكه عنه
These three groups are the elite of the Muhammadan community, and whoever besides them from the sects is in misguidance, even if some of them are judged to have Islam. So the saved one is he whose creed is in accordance with what Ahl al-Sunna have explained, and he follows in practical rulings an imam from the four approved imams. Then the completion of blessing and salvation is in following the path of al-Junayd and his followers after he has firmly established his religion in accordance with what the two aforementioned groups have explained. And among those who followed his path is ... from him.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a concluding statement about the saved sect. It begins by affirming that the three groups mentioned earlier constitute the elite of the Muslim community, while all other sects are misguided—even if some of them are considered part of Islam. The author then lays out three criteria for salvation: first, correct belief ('aqida) in line with Ahl al-Sunna; second, adherence in practical jurisprudence to one of the four recognized imams; and third, the perfection of blessing and salvation comes from following the spiritual path of al-Junayd al-Baghdadi and his followers, after one has already grounded his religion according to the teachings of the first two groups (Ahl al-Sunna in creed and one of the four imams in practice). The phrase 'among those who followed his path' seems to introduce an example, but the text breaks off.

Key Terms
أهل السُّنَّة
الأئمة الأربعة
مسلك الجنيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that mere affiliation with one of the four schools is sufficient without correct creed or spiritual purification.
Correction: The passage requires all three: sound creed, legal following, and Sufi path. None alone is sufficient for complete salvation.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what three things are essential for complete salvation?
A) Following any school of thought, performing good deeds, and avoiding sin.
B) Correct belief on the pattern of Ahl al-Sunna, following a recognized imam in practice, and walking the path of al-Junayd.
C) Merely belonging to the three groups mentioned without any further conditions.
D) Strict asceticism and isolation from society.

Key Takeaway
Complete salvation in traditional Sunni Islam requires correct creed (Ahl al-Sunna), adherence to a recognized legal school, and following the spiritual path of al-Junayd.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that salvation requires three layers: correct creed, following a legal school, and spiritual purification. Which of these layers is weakest in your life today? What is one concrete step you will take this week to strengthen it?
?
Do you rely on your madhab or spiritual practice as a substitute for the other two? How can you ensure your spiritual path is built on sound creed and law, not detached from them?
?
If you were to die tonight, would you be confident that you have fulfilled all three criteria as described by this author? What change in your priorities does this demand starting tomorrow?

The Life and Miracles of Ahmad al-Rifa'i
Biography and miracles of Ahmad al-Rifa'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the revered status of Ahmad al-Rifa'i in Sufism and the types of miracles (karamat) attributed to him in traditional hagiography.

Core Idea
Saints like Ahmad al-Rifa'i are honored for miraculous acts that confirm their spiritual station.

This passage from the coursebook introduces the life and miracles of Ahmad al-Rifa'i, founder of the Rifa'i Sufi order. It draws from biographical sources to narrate extraordinary events that illustrate his closeness to God and the Prophet. The stories serve to inspire devotion and affirm the spiritual authority of the saint.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main claims
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting the key claims about al-Rifa'i's leadership and the wonders associated with him.
Pay attention to the sources cited, like Ibn Khallikan.
2
Examine each miracle and its significance
Go through each story: the melting, the white leaf, the hand from the grave, the garden purchase. Consider what each miracle suggests about his spiritual rank.
Note that these are presented as karamat, not proofs of divinity.
3
Reflect on the purpose of hagiography in Islamic learning
Ask yourself why such accounts are included in a theological coursebook. What lesson about saints (awliya) do they teach?
The passage concludes with his death and succession, reinforcing his legacy.
